Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Fatwa Hierarchy in Dhawi al-Arham Inheritance
States that fatwa follows Imam Muhammad for dhawi al-arham

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the preferred Hanafi opinion on dhawi al-arham inheritance and apply the proximity principle to determine the heir among distant relatives.

Core Idea
Fatwa on dhawi al-arham follows Imam Muhammad, based on proximity, not equality.

When inheriting property, the Hanafi school gives priority to the closest relative among the dhawi al-arham. This lesson examines the rasm al-mufti rule that establishes Imam Muhammad's opinion as the authoritative position, overruling Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti issuing fatwas on inheritance cases involving distant relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rasm al-Mufti Rule
The passage states that scholars have given fatwa on Imam Muhammad's saying. This is the operative rule for inheritance among dhawi al-arham.
This rule is part of the 'mufti hierarchy' — knowing whose opinion to follow in case of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the Hierarchy
Imam Muhammad's opinion is preferred because it aligns with the famous narration of Imam Abu Hanifa. Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is outweighed (marjuh). The fatwa must not follow it.
The famous narration (riwayah) of Imam Abu Hanifa carries more weight than other narrations.
3
Grasp the Proximity Principle
Among dhawi al-arham, the closest to the deceased inherits; the more distant is excluded. This is the core rule for the first category.
Proximity is measured by generational distance, not by degree of kinship as in other systems.
4
Apply the Example
In the given example: a granddaughter (daughter's daughter) is closer than her own son. Hence the granddaughter inherits, and the great-grandson is excluded.
This shows how the rule works in practice: proximity trumps distance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) ذوی الارحام کی میراث کے سلسلے میں علماء نے حضرت امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول پر فتویٰ دیا ہے، امام صاحب صلى الله عليه وسلم کی دو روایتوں میں سے مشہور روایت بھی امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ہی قول کی طرح ہے؛ لہذا اسی پر فتویٰ دیا جائے گا ۔ اِس سلسلے میں امام ابو یوسف کا قول مرجوح ہے، اُس کے مطابق فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا، ذوی الارحام کی مختلف صورتوں میں حضرت امام ابو یوسف صلى الله عليه وسلم اور حضرت امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مابین اختلاف ہے ، جن تمام میں امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول پر ہی فتویٰ ہے۔ مثال سے وضاحت: بہ طور نمونہ ایک مثال پیش کی جاتی ہے، جس کا تعلق ذوی الارحام کی پہلی قسم سے ہے: ذوی الارحام کی پہلی قسم میں وہ لوگ ہیں، جو میت کی طرف منسوب ہیں ؛ یعنی میت کی بیٹی ، پوتی کی اولاد ( نواسہ، نواسی، پڑپوتا، پڑپوتی اور ان کی اولاد ) ۔ ان میں میراث تقسیم کرنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے: (۱) اگر ان میں کوئی میت سے قریب ہو، اور کوئی دور ہو، تو جو قریب ہو، وہ وارث ہو گا اور جو دور ہو ، وہ محروم ہو گا ۔ جیسے کوئی نواسی ہو، اور کوئی نواسی کا لڑکا ہو ، تو نواسی کو وارث قرار دیا جائے گا، نہ کہ نواسی کے لڑکے کو۔
(3) Regarding the inheritance of dhawi al-arham, scholars have given fatwa on the saying of Hadrat Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him). Among the two narrations of Imam Sahib (peace be upon him), the famous narration is also similar to the saying of Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him); therefore, fatwa will be given on this. In this matter, the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is outweighed, and fatwa will not be given according to it. In various cases of dhawi al-arham, there is difference between Hadrat Imam Abu Yusuf (peace be upon him) and Hadrat Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him), and in all of them, fatwa is on the saying of Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him). Explanation with example: As a specimen, an example is presented which relates to the first category of dhawi al-arham: The first category of dhawi al-arham are those who are related to the deceased; i.e., the daughter of the deceased, the children of the granddaughter (grandson, granddaughter, great-grandson, great-granddaughter and their children). The method of distributing inheritance among them is: (1) If among them some are closer and some are farther, then the closer one will inherit and the farther one will be excluded. For example, if there is a granddaughter and a son of the granddaughter, then the granddaughter will be considered the heir, not the son of the granddaughter.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm al-mufti rule concerning the inheritance of dhawi al-arham (distant relatives who are not Quranic heirs nor agnates). It states that scholars have given fatwa according to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's opinion. Imam Muhammad's opinion is also supported by the famous narration of Imam Abu Hanifa (referred to as Imam Sahib). Thus, fatwa is according to Imam Muhammad, and Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is considered outweighed. The passage then provides an example from the first category of dhawi al-arham: those who are descendants of the deceased's daughters or granddaughters. The principle is proximity: the closer relative inherits, and the more distant is excluded. For instance, a granddaughter is closer than the granddaughter's son, so she inherits.

Key Terms
ذوی الارحام (dhawi al-arham): Distant relatives who are neither Quranic heirs nor agnates (asaba)
مرجوح (marjuh): Outweighed, the opinion that is not followed because a stronger proof supports another view.
مشہور روایت (mashhur riwayah): The famous narration attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, considered more reliable within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rasm al-mufti rule for dhawi al-arham inheritance, whose saying is followed?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa's
B) Imam Abu Yusuf's
C) Imam Muhammad's
D) All three equally depending on the case

Key Takeaway
Fatwa on dhawi al-arham inheritance follows Imam Muhammad's proximity principle, and the closest relative inherits to the exclusion of the more distant.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Inheritance of Dhawi al-Arham (First Category)
Ruling on inheritance of dhawi al-arham with fatwa preference for Imam Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi fatwa on inheritance distribution among dhawi al-arham of the first category, distinguishing between Imam Muhammad's mufta bihi opinion and Imam Abu Yusuf's marjuh view.

Core Idea
For dhawi al-arham inheritance, Imam Muhammad's opinion is the mufta bihi: closer excludes farther, and primary heir descendants exclude others.

This passage addresses a key part of Hanafi inheritance law: how muftis should rule on the shares of distant kindred (dhawi al-arham) related through female links. The text clarifies that although Imam Abu Yusuf had differing views, the fatwa relies on Imam Muhammad's rulings. Understanding this hierarchy of authority is essential for a mufti when issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the school's hierarchy
Note that the passage explicitly states that fatwa follows Imam Muhammad's opinion, not Abu Yusuf's. The 'famous narration' also agrees with Imam Muhammad. Recognize this as a tarjih mechanism.
Intra-madhhab preference is a core concept in rasm al-mufti.
2
State the three distribution rules
Read the rules: (1) Closer in relation excludes farther. (2) Equally distant: descendant of a primary heir excludes descendant of dhawi al-arham. (3) Equally distant and same lineage: if roots share gender, male:female 2:1 by consensus; if roots differ in gender, there is dispute (Imam Muhammad vs Abu Yusuf).
Write down each rule and its example.
3
Distinguish agreed vs. disputed cases
Rule 3 part (b) introduces a case where the roots (the connecting ancestors) have different genders. The passage gives an incomplete example of a daughter of a grandson vs. son of a granddaughter. Realize that this is the point of ikhtilaf between the two imams.
The mufta bihi in this disputed case is Imam Muhammad's ruling, though the passage does not state his specific decision.
4
Apply the rules to a fresh scenario
Take a hypothetical: Deceased leaves a daughter's son (grandson) and a son of a daughter's daughter (great-grandson). According to rule 1, the closer relative (grandson) inherits; the great-grandson is excluded. If both are equally distant (e.g., two sons of two daughters), then under rule 2, since both are descendants of primary heirs (daughters), they inherit with the male taking double.
Practice with simple cases to internalize the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذوی الارحام کی میراث کے سلسلے میں امام محمدی کا قول مفتی یہ ہے
(۳) ذوی الارحام کے مابین تقسیم میراث کے طریقے کے سلسلے میں علماء نے حضرت امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول پر فتویٰ دیا ہے، امام صاحب صلى الله عليه وسلم کی دو روایتوں میں سے مشہور روایت بھی امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ہی قول کی طرح ہے؛ لہذا اسی پر فتویٰ دیا جائے گا ۔ اِس سلسلے میں امام ابو یوسف کا قول مرجوح ہے، اُس کے مطابق فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا، ذوی الارحام کی مختلف صورتوں میں حضرت امام ابو یوسف صلى الله عليه وسلم اور حضرت امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مابین اختلاف ہے ، جن تمام میں امام محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول پر ہی فتویٰ ہے۔
مثال سے وضاحت
بہ طور نمونہ ایک مثال پیش کی جاتی ہے، جس کا تعلق ذوی الارحام کی پہلی قسم سے ہے:
ذوی الارحام کی پہلی قسم میں وہ لوگ ہیں، جو میت کی طرف منسوب ہیں ؛ یعنی میت کی بیٹی ، پوتی کی اولاد ( نواسہ، نواسی، پڑپوتا، پڑپوتی اور ان کی اولاد ) ۔ ان میں میراث تقسیم کرنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے: (۱) اگر ان میں کوئی میت سے قریب ہو، اور کوئی دور ہو، تو جو قریب ہو، وہ وارث ہو گا اور جو دور ہو ، وہ محروم ہو گا ۔ جیسے کوئی نواسی ہو، اور کوئی نواسی کا لڑکا ہو ، تو نواسی کو وارث قرار دیا جائے گا، نہ کہ نواسی کے لڑکے کو۔
(۲) اگر دونوں برابر درجے کے ہوں، میت سے نہ کوئی قریب ہو، نہ کوئی بعید ہو ؟ مگر کوئی وارث کی اولاد ہو اور کوئی ذوی الارحام کی اولاد ہو، تو جو وارث کی اولاد ہوگی ، اُس کو وارث قرار دیا جائے گا اور جو ذوی الارحام کی اولا د ہوگی ،اُس کو محروم قرار دیا جائے گا۔ جیسے ہوتی کی لڑکی اور نواسے کا لڑکا تو اس میں ہوتی کی لڑکی کو وارث قرار دیا جائے گا، نہ کہ نواسے کے لڑکے کو۔
(۳) اور اگر سب برابر درجے کے ہوں، نیز سب کے سب یا تو وارث کی اولاد ہوں یا سب ذوی الارحام کی اولاد ہوں ، تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں: . ان کے اصول صفت ذکورت اور انوشت میں متحد ہوں، تو اس صورت میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں۔
. ذوی الارحام کی پہلی قسم کے اصول صفت ذکورت اور انوشت میں متحد نہ ہوں ؛ بل کہ اُن میں کسی کے اصول مذکر تو کسی کے مؤنث ہوں۔ پہلی صورت کی مثال میت کی ایک بیٹی کا بیٹا، دوسری بیٹی کی بیٹی ؛ اس صورت میں بالا تفاق بیٹی کے بیٹے کو دو حصے اور بیٹی کی بیٹی کو ایک حصہ دیا جائے گا؛ اس لیے کہ دونوں کے اصول یعنی بیٹی صفت اُ نوشت میں متحد ہیں۔
دوسری صورت کی مثال جو کہ اختلافی ہے، یہ ہے کہ ایک نواسے کی لڑکی، دوسری نواسی کا لڑکا ہو۔ مثلاً : عائشہ کی دو بیٹیاں تھیں: (۱) فاطمہ (۲) رقیہ: فاطمہ کا ایک لڑکا تھا، جس کا نام زید تھا، اس کی ایک بیٹی ہے، اس کا نام ہاجرہ ہے۔ اسی طرح عائشہ کی دوسری بیٹی رقیہ کی بھی ایک بیٹی تھی ، اس کا نام ام کلثوم تھا، ام کلثوم کا ایک بیٹا ہے، اُس کا نام عبد اللہ ہے۔ جس وقت عائشہ کا انتقال ہوا، اُس سے پہلے عائشہ کی دونوں بیٹیوں فاطمہ اور رقیہ ؛ اسی طرح فاطمہ کے بیٹے زید اور رقیہ کی بیٹی ام
Regarding the inheritance of dhawi al-arham, the opinion of Imam Muhammad on which the mufti acts is: (3) Concerning the method of dividing inheritance among dhawi al-arham, the scholars have given fatwa according to the saying of Imam Muhammad, may peace be upon him. Among the two narrations from Imam Sahib, the famous narration also resembles the saying of Imam Muhammad; therefore fatwa will be given accordingly. In this matter, the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is considered weak (marjuh); fatwa will not be given according to it. In various cases of dhawi al-arham, there is a difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad; in all of them, fatwa is according to the saying of Imam Muhammad. Explanation with an example: By way of example, one case is presented which relates to the first category of dhawi al-arham: The first category of dhawi al-arham includes those who are related to the deceased through a female link, i.e., daughter of the deceased, descendants of a granddaughter (grandson, granddaughter, great-grandson, great-granddaughter and their descendants). The method of distributing inheritance among them is: (1) If among them one is closer to the deceased and one is farther, then the one who is closer will inherit and the one who is farther will be excluded. For example, if there is a granddaughter and a son of that granddaughter, then the granddaughter will be given inheritance, not the son of the granddaughter. (2) If both are of the same degree, neither closer nor farther from the deceased, but one is a descendant of a primary heir (warith) and the other is a descendant of a dhawi al-arham relative, then the descendant of the primary heir will be given inheritance and the descendant of the dhawi al-arham will be excluded. For example, a daughter of a [primary heir?] and a son of a grandson: in this case, the daughter of the [primary heir?] will be given inheritance, not the son of the grandson. (3) And if all are of the same degree, and all are either descendants of a primary heir or all are descendants of dhawi al-arham, then there are two situations: (a) If their roots (asl) are united in the attribute of masculinity and femininity, then in this case there is no disagreement. (b) If the roots of the first category of dhawi al-arham are not united in the attribute of masculinity and femininity, but rather among them some roots are male and some female. Example of the first situation: a son of one daughter of the deceased and a daughter of another daughter; in this case, by agreement, the son of the daughter will be given two shares and the daughter of the daughter one share, because their roots, that is, the daughters, are united in the attribute of femininity. Example of the second situation, which is disputed, is: one is the daughter of a grandson, and the other is the son of a granddaughter. For instance: Aisha had two daughters: (1) Fatima and (2) Ruqayya. Fatima had a son named Zaid, and he had a daughter named Hajira. Similarly, Aisha's second daughter Ruqayya had a daughter named Umm Kulthum, and Umm Kulthum had a son named Abdullah. When Aisha passed away, before that Aisha's both daughters Fatima and Ruqayya; similarly Fatima's son Zaid and Ruqayya's daughter Umm...
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the methodology of inheritance distribution among dhawi al-arham (distant kindred), specifically the first category, which includes descendants through female links. The text establishes that the fatwa (official ruling for muftis) is based on the opinion of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, not that of Imam Abu Yusuf. The author explains that even among the two narrations from Imam Muhammad, the more famous one aligns with his own explicit statement, so it is relied upon. Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is considered weak (marjuh) and not acted upon. The text then provides three rules for distribution within the first category: (1) proximity in relation to the deceased (closer excludes farther); (2) when equally distant, descendant of a primary heir (e.g., a child of the deceased) excludes a descendant of dhawi al-arham (e.g., a child of a grandchild); (3) when all are equally distant and all are from the same lineage (either all from primary heirs or all from dhawi al-arham), then if their roots (the immediate ancestors connecting them to the deceased) share the same gender (both male or both female), there is consensus: the male takes twice the female's share. If the roots differ in gender, there is a dispute among the imams, and the text gives an example involving the daughter of a grandson and the son of a granddaughter. Unfortunately, the example is cut off. The ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and emphasizes the methodology of tarjih (preference) among the founding imams.

Key Terms
ذوی الارحام (Dhawi al-arham): Distant kindred who inherit after primary heirs and agnates; specifically in this passage, those related through female links (e.g., daughter's descendants).
مرجوح (Marjuh): The weaker or less preferred opinion that is not followed in fatwa, as opposed to the rajih (preferred) opinion.
اصول (Usul): The roots or immediate ancestors through whom the claimant is connected to the deceased; e.g., for a child of a daughter, the root is the daughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the inheritance of dhawi al-arham of the first category, if two claimants are equally distant but one is the descendant of a primary heir and the other is the descendant of a dhawi al-arham relative, who inherits?
A) The descendant of the primary heir.
B) The descendant of the dhawi al-arham.
C) Both inherit equally.
D) The one with the male ancestor.

Key Takeaway
For fatwa on dhawi al-arham inheritance of the first category, Imam Muhammad's opinion is the mufta bihi, with the principle that closer excludes farther and descendants of primary heirs take precedence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner
6 min
Preference of Istihsan Over Qiyas in Fatwa
Rule that istihsan takes precedence over qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-istihsan yuqaddam 'ala al-qiyas' to identify the mufta bihi ruling when two conflicting opinions are derived from qiyas and istihsan.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fatwa, when qiyas and istihsan conflict, the ruling based on istihsan prevails.

This passage introduces a key rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the preference of istihsan over qiyas. The rule governs how a mufti resolves contradictions arising from different methods of reasoning. The example of funeral prayer on a riding animal illustrates the practical application where qiyas would permit but istihsan forbids.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the Maxim
State the Arabic maxim 'al-istihsan yuqaddam 'ala al-qiyas' and its English meaning: 'Istihsan is given preference over qiyas.' This is the core rule.
2
Understand the Ta‘lil (Rationale)
The text says istihsan is preferred because it is based on stronger evidence (qawwat al-dalil). Recognize that istihsan is not arbitrary but grounded in stronger proof.
3
Recognize the Scope
This rule applies whenever a case yields two contradictory rulings: one from qiyas and one from istihsan. It is not limited to a specific chapter of fiqh.
4
Apply to the Example
Work through the funeral prayer example: qiyas compares it to du'a (supplication), thus permitting riding; istihsan considers the presence of takbirat al-tahrimah, making it a form of salat, thus forbidding riding. Note the different reasoning.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling for fatwa) is the one derived from istihsan. In the example, the fatwa would be that funeral prayer on a riding animal is not permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استحسان کو قیاس پر ترجیح ہوگی (۴) اگر کسی مسئلے میں ایک حکم قیاس کے مطابق ہو، اور دوسرا استحسان کے مطابق، تو قوت دلیل کی بنیاد پر استحسان والا قول راجح ہوگا ، اسی کے مطابق فتویٰ دیا جائے گا۔ جیسے : سواری پر چلتے ہوئے نماز جنازہ کے متعلق اگر قیاس پر نظر رکھی جائے ، تو معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نماز جنازہ سواری پر جائز ہونی چاہیے؛ اس لیے کہ وہ در اصل نماز نہیں ؛ بل کہ دعا ہے اور دعا ہر حالت میں جائز ہے، اس کے لیے سواری یا پیدل کی کوئی قید نہیں۔ اس کے برخلاف استحسان کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ سواری کی حالت میں نماز جنازہ جائز نہ ہو ؛ اس لیے کہ تکبیر تحریمہ وغیرہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے، اُس
Istihsan will be given preference over qiyas. (4) If in a matter there is one ruling according to qiyas and another according to istihsan, then based on the strength of evidence, the opinion based on istihsan will be preponderant, and fatwa will be given accordingly. For example: concerning funeral prayer (janazah) while riding, if one looks from the perspective of qiyas, it appears that funeral prayer on a riding animal should be permissible, because it is not actually a prayer but rather a supplication, and supplication is permissible in every state; there is no restriction of riding or walking for it. On the contrary, istihsan requires that funeral prayer while riding is not permissible, because of the presence of takbirat al-tahrimah etc. [in it].
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage states a rasm al-mufti rule: when a case presents two contradictory rulings—one derived from qiyas (analogical reasoning) and one from istihsan (juristic preference, which is a stronger form of reasoning in Hanafi usul)—the mufti must give fatwa according to istihsan because it is based on stronger evidence. The rule is numbered (4), indicating it is one of the principles in the text. The example given is the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) performed while riding an animal. Qiyas, comparing it to ordinary supplication (du'a), would allow it because du'a has no conditions of standing or facing. However, istihsan forbids it because the funeral prayer includes takbirat al-tahrimah (the opening takbir), which makes it a form of salat, and salat on a riding animal without excuse is not permissible. The passage is incomplete in this window; it continues onto the next page. This rule is fundamental in Hanafi fatwa methodology: istihsan overrides qiyas when there is a conflict.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from qiyas for a stronger evidence or custom
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause ('illah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule, which source takes precedence in case of conflict between qiyas and istihsan?
A) Qiyas
B) Istihsan
C) Both are equal
D) Neither, mujtahid chooses

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, when qiyas and istihsan conflict, the ruling based on istihsan is adopted because it is supported by stronger evidence.

Deviation from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah Not Permissible for the Mufti
Methodological rule on the hierarchy of transmitted rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a mufti must follow Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, and identify the only circumstance where a shādhdh narration may be adopted (when the later mashā'ikh have given fatwa upon it).

Core Idea
A mufti must rule by Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah unless the later mashā'ikh have shifted fatwa to a shādhdh narration.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti establishes a key hierarchy in Hanafi fatwa. The mufti is bound to follow the well-known transmitted rulings (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah) and the preferences of the later authorities (mashā'ikh). He may not arbitrarily choose a weaker transmission unless the mashā'ikh have already adopted it. Understanding this rule prevents common errors in fatwa selection and ensures consistency with the school's authoritative positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary rule
The mufti must adhere to Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and the preferences of the mashā'ikh. This is the default obligation.
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah refers to the core works of Imam Muhammad.
2
Recognize the exception
Deviation to a shādhdh narration is allowed only if the later mashā'ikh have themselves given fatwa on that narration.
This transfers authority to the later consensus.
3
Examine the first example: multiple missed prayers
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah gives choice for adhan and iqamah in subsequent prayers; a shādhdh narration says no adhan. The mufti follows Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.
This illustrates the default rule.
4
Analyze the second example: woman's palm as 'awrah
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah includes the palm, but Imam Qadi Khan (a later mash'ikh) ruled it is not 'awrah. Fatwa is given on Qadi Khan's view, showing the mashā'ikh's tarjīḥ can override Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.
This is the exception in action.

Deviation from Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is not permissible. (5) This has been mentioned multiple times: that following Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and the preferences of the mashā'ikh is obligatory. It is not permissible for general muftis, without any reasonable excuse, to act upon or give fatwa according to a shādhdh narration when Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah exists. For example, from Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him), in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, and the school of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that if multiple missed prayers accumulate, then for the first prayer both adhan and iqamah will be said, and for the subsequent prayers there is choice: either both adhan and iqamah or just iqamah. In contrast, from Imam Muhammad in non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah it is explicitly transmitted that for any prayer after the first, adhan should not be recited. Here the mufti will give fatwa on Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and will not opt for the non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. Unless the mashā'ikh have, for some reason, given fatwa according to the shādhdh narration, then it is another matter. For example, Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is that the outer part of a woman's palm is included in the 'awrah, while Imam Qadi Khan wrote that it is not 'awrah. This saying is non-Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, yet fatwa is given upon it. Yes! If the issue is [incomplete]
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning the authority of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah in the Hanafi school. It states that a general mufti must follow the rulings of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah (the core transmitted works of Imam Muhammad) and the preferred positions of the later mashā'ikh. He may not act upon or give fatwa according to a shādhdh (irregular) narration without a valid excuse. The author gives an example: when multiple missed prayers are made up, Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah says that for the first prayer both adhan and iqamah are recited, and for subsequent prayers there is choice. A shādhdh narration says that adhan should not be recited for any subsequent prayer. The mufti must follow Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. However, there is an exception: if the later mashā'ikh have themselves given fatwa according to a shādhdh narration, then it can be followed. The example given is the 'awrah of a woman's palm: Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah includes it, but Imam Qadi Khan (a later authority) ruled it is not 'awrah, and fatwa is given on that. This shows that the mufti must know both the main transmitted rulings and the later preferences of the mashā'ikh.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The explicit, well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six core books (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.).
شاذ روایت (shādhdh riwāyah): An irregular or less authentic transmission that contradicts Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.
مشائخ (mashā'ikh): The later authoritative scholars of the Hanafi school, especially the muta'akhkhirūn (later scholars) who weighed and preferred certain rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever the shādhdh narration seems more reasonable.
B) Only if the later mashā'ikh have given fatwa on that shādhdh narration.
C) Never; Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah must always be followed.
D) Only in cases of necessity or public interest.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must always follow Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah unless the later mashā'ikh have collectively adopted a contrary view.

Choosing the Stronger Evidence Among Multiple Narrations
Rule for preferring stronger riwayah in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm al-mufti rule for preferring the stronger dalil when multiple riwayat exist, using the example of ta'dil al-arkan.

Core Idea
When multiple narrations from an imam conflict, the mufti must follow the one with the stronger evidence, not mere frequency.

A mufti often encounters multiple narrations attributed to the same imam on a single issue. This passage from a rasm al-mufti work lays down a critical rule: the mufti must evaluate the evidence (dalil) supporting each narration, whether it is a primary text (nass), consensus (ijma), or analogical reasoning (qiyas), and choose the strongest. The example of ta'dil al-arkan in prayer illustrates how this rule works in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The passage states: when multiple riwayat exist from an imam on one issue, adopt the narration that is stronger in terms of evidence (dalil). This overrides reliance on mere frequency or convenience.
The rule applies regardless of whether the dalil is nass, ijma, or qiyas.
2
Examine the preliminary rule on nadir al-riwaya
If a ruling is not found in well-known (zahir al-riwaya) texts but only in a rare narration (nadir al-riwaya), acting upon it is permitted but determined. This introduces a hierarchy of sources.
Nadir al-riwaya is not automatically rejected; it can be used when no other evidence is available.
3
Apply to the example of ta'dil al-arkan
The passage uses the case of proper straightening of postures in prayer. There are multiple narrations: fard from Abu Yusuf, sunna from one view, wajib from another. The opinion of wujub is chosen because it is found in authoritative matn texts (Hidayah, Kanz, Wiqayah) and is supported by the hadith 'Go back and pray, for you have not prayed.'
This shows how the strength of dalil is assessed: both textual authenticity (in reliable matn) and prophetic evidence.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a mufti follows the stronger view (wujub), ta'dil is obligatory and leaving it requires compensation (sajdah sahw). If the weaker view (sunna) were followed, the prayer would be valid without ta'dil, but that would contradict the stronger evidence.
The mufti must be aware of the difference in ruling to guide the questioner correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرواية" میں نہ ملے اور مذہب کی کسی " نادر الرواية " میں پایا جائے ، تو اس پر عمل کرنا متعین ہوگا۔
کسی قول پر فتوی دینے میں دلیل کو نظر انداز نہیں کیا جائے گا
(۶) اگر کسی امام سے ایک ہی مسئلے میں متعدد روایتیں منقول ہوں، تو جو روایت دلیل کے اعتبار سے مضبوط ہو گی ، اُسے اختیار کیا جائے گا، دلیل خواہ وہ نص ہو یا اجتماع یا اجتہاد وقیاس دلیل سے قطع نظر کسی بھی روایت پر فتوی دے دینا درست نہ ہوگا؛ بل کہ فتوے کے وقت مختلف روایتوں میں جس کی دلیل مضبوط ہوگی ، اُسی کے مطابق فتویٰ دینا ہوگا ، جیسے: نماز میں تعدیل ارکان امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک فرض ہے، حضرات طرفین سے اس سلسلے میں دور و استیں ملتی ہیں: ایک کے مطابق سنت اور ایک مطابق واجب ہے؛ وجوب کا قول روایت کے اعتبار سے بھی مضبوط ہے؛ اس لیے کہ یہ قول هداية ،كنز، وقاية" وغیرہ متونِ معتبرہ میں ہے، جس کی بنیاد پر اسے ضمنی تصیح حاصل ہے اور دلیل: ارْجِعُ فَصَلِّ فَإِنَّكَ لَمُ تُصلّ" کے اعتبار سے بھی مضبوط ہے؛ اس لیے فتویٰ اسی پر دیا جاتا ہے۔
If [a ruling] is not found in the [well-known] narrations and is found in a "nadir al-riwaya" of the madhhab, then acting upon it becomes determined. When giving a fatwa on any statement, the evidence should not be ignored. (6) If multiple narrations are transmitted from an imam regarding one issue, then the narration that is stronger in terms of evidence will be adopted. Whether the evidence is a text (nass) or consensus (ijma) or ijtihad and qiyas, it is not correct to issue a fatwa on any narration disregarding the evidence; rather, at the time of giving fatwa, among the different narrations, the one whose evidence is stronger must be given according to it. For example: the proper straightening of postures (ta'dil al-arkan) in prayer is fard according to Imam Abu Yusuf; from the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) there are two views: according to one it is sunna and according to one it is wajib. The opinion of obligation (wujub) is stronger in terms of narration because it is found in reliable texts like Hidayah, Kanz, Wiqayah, etc., which gives it implicit verification, and it is also strong in terms of evidence: the hadith "Go back and pray, for you have not prayed." Therefore, fatwa is given on this.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental rasm rule for muftis: when there are multiple narrations (riwayat) attributed to an imam (such as Abu Hanifa or his students), the mufti must not simply choose arbitrarily. Instead, he must evaluate the strength of the evidence (dalil) supporting each narration. The rule applies whether the dalil is a primary text (nass), consensus (ijma), or analogical reasoning (qiyas/ijtihad). The example given is the issue of ta'dil al-arkan (performing each posture of prayer with proper stillness). Imam Abu Yusuf considered it fard (obligatory), while the other two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) had conflicting reports: one says sunna, one says wajib. The text explains that the opinion of wujub (obligation) is stronger because it appears in authoritative matn texts (Hidayah, Kanz, Wiqayah) and is supported by the famous hadith of the man who prayed incorrectly. Hence, the mufti should give fatwa on this stronger view. The passage also includes a preliminary statement: if a ruling is not found in the well-known (zahir al-riwaya) texts but only in a rare transmission (nadir al-riwaya), acting upon it is determined (i.e., it can be followed under certain conditions, but this needs further elaboration).

Key Terms
تعديل أركان (ta'dil al-arkan): The act of performing each posture in prayer (standing, bowing, prostrating, sitting) with full stillness and proper positioning.
نادر الرواية (nadir al-riwaya): A rare or less frequently transmitted narration within the Hanafi school, often transmitted by a single student of the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The narration with stronger evidence (dalil)
C) The narration that is easiest for the public
D) The narration of Imam Abu Yusuf always takes precedence

Key Takeaway
A mufti must always evaluate the strength of the evidence behind each narration and give fatwa on the strongest, regardless of frequency or ease.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

6 min
The Retracted Opinion is Like Abrogated
States that a retracted opinion (marju' 'anhu) is treated as mansukh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a retracted opinion (marju' 'anhu) is invalid for fatwa and identify the operative later opinion.

Core Idea
A mujtahid's retracted opinion is invalid for fatwa, like abrogated text; only the later opinion governs.

When a mujtahid (such as Imam Abu Hanifa) changes his view, the earlier view no longer carries authority. This lesson explains why the retracted opinion is akin to a mansukh ruling and how a mufti must determine and follow the later, adopted position.

Guided Path
1
State the Rule
Identify the rule: the retracted opinion (marju' 'anhu) is like an abrogated ruling (mansukh) — it cannot be acted upon.
This is a binding rasm al-mufti principle.
2
Understand the Analogy
Analyze the qiyas: asl (mansukh) is a ruling that is no longer valid due to abrogation; far' (marju' 'anhu) is an opinion that is no longer valid due to retraction. The illa is that both are invalidated by a later authoritative action.
The analogy is based on the shared consequence: inapplicability for fatwa.
3
Apply to the Example
Examine the given case: Imam Abu Hanifa initially held that wiping over khuffain (socks) is not permitted, then retracted and allowed it. The earlier opinion is marju' 'anhu and cannot be followed.
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held permissibility throughout, but the key is the Imam's own retraction.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The mufti must seek the later, adopted opinion of the mujtahid and base the fatwa on that. Any fatwa on the retracted opinion is impermissible.
This rule prevents reliance on outdated positions within the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸) اس شعر میں علامہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہ ضابطہ بیان کیا کہ جس قول سے مجتہد رجوع کرلے، وہ منسوخ کے درجے میں ہو جاتا ہے، عام مفتیوں کے لیے اُس پر عمل کرنا یا اُس کے مطابق فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں، اب تو بس اُس قول کو تلاش کرنا ضروری ہے ، جس کی طرف مجتہد نے رجوع کیا ہے ، اُسی پر عمل ہوگا ، اُسی کے مطابق فتوی دیا جائے گا؛ کیوں کہ مرجوع عنہ قول منسوخ کی طرح ہے؛ لہذا جس طرح منسوخ پر عمل اور فتویٰ جائز نہیں، اسی طرح مرجوع عنہ پر عمل اور فتویٰ درست نہیں ، جیسے شخین جراب پر حضرات صاحبین مسح کے جواز کے قائل تھے، جب کہ امام صاحب پہلے اس پر مسح کے عدم جواز کے قائل تھے ، پھر آپ نے عدم جواز کے قول سے رجوع فرمالیا اور اس پر سج کے جواز کا فتوی دیا؛ لہذا اب امام صاحب صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اُس مرجوع عنہ قول کے مطابق فتوی نہیں دیا جائے گا۔
(8) In this couplet, Allamah [the author] has stated this rule: An opinion from which the mujtahid has retracted becomes like an abrogated (mansukh) ruling. It is not permissible for general muftis to act upon it or give fatwa according to it. Now it is necessary to search for the opinion to which the mujtahid retracted; only that opinion will be acted upon and fatwa will be given according to it. Because the retracted opinion (marju' 'anhu) is like an abrogated ruling. Just as acting upon and giving fatwa on a mansukh is not permissible, similarly acting upon and giving fatwa on a retracted opinion is not correct. For example: The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held the view of permissibility of wiping over socks (khuffain), while Imam Abu Hanifa initially held the view of impermissibility. Then he retracted from the opinion of impermissibility and gave a fatwa of permissibility. Therefore, now no fatwa can be given according to that retracted opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage establishes another important rasm rule: when a mujtahid (such as Imam Abu Hanifa) retracts an earlier opinion and adopts a new one, the earlier opinion is no longer valid for fatwa. It is treated like a mansukh (abrogated) ruling. The mufti must seek out the later, adopted opinion and base his fatwa on that. The example given is the issue of wiping over military socks (al-khuffain al-jiraab? actually leather socks/socks). Initially, Imam Abu Hanifa did not allow wiping over them, but later he retracted that and permitted it. Thus, the earlier opinion of impermissibility cannot be followed. This rule ensures that the mufti does not cling to outdated views that the school's founder himself rejected.

Key Terms
مرجوع عنہ (marju' 'anhu): The opinion from which the mujtahid has retracted; it is no longer a valid basis for fatwa.
منسوخ (mansukh): A ruling that has been abrogated by a later evidence; no longer applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is like an abrogated (mansukh) ruling
C) It was only a minority opinion
D) It was never transmitted correctly

Key Takeaway
A retracted opinion (marju' 'anhu) is invalid for fatwa; only the later, adopted opinion of the mujtahid is operative.

Implicit Authentication by Inclusion in Authoritative Texts
A rasm al-mufti rule establishing implicit authentication via inclusion in authoritative texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule of implicit authentication to determine the mufta bihi position and prioritize rulings from authoritative texts over commentaries.

Core Idea
Inclusion in the authoritative matun is implicit authentication; no fatwa is given against them without explicit authentication.

The Hanafi madhhab has a structured hierarchy for determining the relied-upon position. One key principle is that a ruling's presence in the standard mutun—such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and others—is itself a certification of its authenticity. In this lesson, we examine how implicit authentication works and how it affects fatwa preference, using the example of a blind person's testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The passage states that a saying appearing in the authoritative mutun is implicitly authenticated because the authors committed to transmitting only authentic sayings.
This rule is a cornerstone of Hanafi usul al-ifta.
2
Understand the rationale
The authors of the mutun (e.g., al-Marghinani, al-Quduri) specifically undertook to report only sahih positions. Thus, inclusion in their works serves as a guarantee of authenticity.
This is known as 'dimni tas-hih' – implicit authentication.
3
Apply the hierarchy
Priority order: first, the agreed-upon sayings in the mutun; second, sayings in commentaries; third, sayings of the mashayikh. A saying outside the mutun is not followed unless explicitly authenticated.
Explicit authentication overrides implicit authentication.
4
Examine the example
All mutun agree that a blind person's testimony is not accepted. A commentary reports via Imam Zufar that it is accepted in hearing cases. Since this contradicts the mutun and lacks explicit authentication, the mutun ruling prevails.
This illustrates the practical application of the rule.

(۹) اس شعر میں علامہ شامی فرمارہے ہیں کہ جو قول متن کی معتبر کتابوں میں موجود ہو ، فتویٰ اسی پر دیا جائے گا ؛ اس لیے کہ کسی قول کا متونِ معتبرہ مثلاً : "بداية المبتدي، مختصر القدوري ، النقاية، وقاية، كنز الدقائق، ملتقى الأبحر" وغیرہ کتابوں میں آجانا ، یہ اس قول کی ضمنی والتزامی تصحیح ہے، ان کتابوں کے مصنفین نے خاص طور پر صیح اقوال نقل کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے لہذا جو قول متونِ معتبرہ سے باہر ہوں گے، متون غیر معتبرہ میں، شروحات میں ، فتاویٰ میں؟ اُن پر فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ ہاں! اگر متون معتبرہ کے علاوہ قول کی صراحاً تصحیح وارد ہو، تو پھر ایسی صورت میں اسی پر فتوی دیا جائے گا؛ کیوں کہ صریح تصحیح التزامی صحیح پر رائج ہوتی ہے۔ مثال کے طور پر مذہب کے سبھی متون متفق ہیں کہ نا بینا شخص کی گواہی پر فیصلہ نہیں کیا جائے گا، جب کہ شروحات وغیرہ میں امام صاحب کی ایک روایت امام زفر کے واسطے سے، نقل کی گئی ہے کہ جن معاملات کا تعلق محض سماع سے ہے اور اُن میں آنکھوں سے مشاہدے کی ضرورت نہیں، اُن میں نابینا کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی ، شروح کی یہ روایت متون کے خلاف ہے اور اس پر مشایخ کے فتوے کی صراحت بھی نہیں ہے؛ لہذا اُصولاً متون کی روایت پر فتویٰ دیا جائے گا اور یہ کہا جائے گا کہ نا بینا کی گواہی معتبر نہیں۔ خلاصہ کلام ! جس قول پر متون متفق ہوں، وہی مفتی بہ اور معتمد علیہ ہوگا، اُس کے بعد دوسرا نمبر اُن اقوال کا ہو گا، جو شروحات میں مذکور ہوں گے، تیسرا نمبر مشائخ
(9) In this couplet, Allamah Shami says: The saying that is present in the authoritative texts (mutun), fatwa will be given according to it, because the appearance of a saying in authoritative texts such as Bidayat al-Mubtadi, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Nuqayah, Wiqayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, Multaqa al-Abhur, etc., is an implicit and committed authentication of that saying. The authors of these books have specifically committed to transmitting authentic sayings. Therefore, a saying that is outside the authoritative texts, in non-authoritative texts, in commentaries, in fatwa collections, fatwa will not be given according to them. Yes, if explicit authentication of a saying occurs outside the authoritative texts, then in that case fatwa will be given according to it, because explicit authentication overrides implicit authentication. For example, all the authoritative texts of the madhhab agree that the testimony of a blind person will not be accepted. However, in commentaries, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifah via Imam Zufar is reported that in matters purely related to hearing, where eyesight is not required, the testimony of a blind person will be accepted. This narration in the commentaries contradicts the texts, and there is no explicit fatwa of the mashayikh upon it. Therefore, in principle, fatwa will be given according to the narration of the texts, and it will be said that the testimony of a blind person is not reliable. Summary: The saying upon which the authoritative texts agree is the mufta bihi and mu'tamad. After that, second rank belongs to sayings mentioned in commentaries, third rank belongs to the mashayikh...
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents another critical rasm al-mufti rule: the authoritative status of sayings that appear in the standard matun (foundational texts) of the Hanafi madhhab. The rule establishes that inclusion in these texts constitutes implicit authentication (tas-hih dimni) because the authors (such as al-Marghinani, al-Quduri, al-Nasafi, etc.) committed themselves to transmitting only sahih (authentic) opinions. Therefore, fatwa must be based on what these matun agree upon. Sayings found only in commentaries, fatwa collections, or non-standard works are not to be given fatwa unless there is explicit authentication from the later authorities. The author gives an example: The matun uniformly state that a blind person's testimony is not accepted. A contrary view reported via Imam Zufar appears in commentaries, but since it contradicts the matun and lacks explicit authentication by the mashayikh, it is not adopted. Finally, the author outlines a hierarchy: first, the agreed-upon sayings in the matun; second, sayings in commentaries; third, sayings of the mashayikh (later authorities). This prioritization is essential for a mufti to correctly determine the mu'tamad (reliable) position of the madhhab.

Key Terms
متون معتبرہ (mutun mu'tabarah): Authoritative foundational texts of the Hanafi madhhab, such as Bidayah, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, etc., whose authors committed to transmitting only authentic rulings.
ضمنی تصحیح (dimni tas-hih): Implicit authentication: the fact that a ruling appears in the authoritative texts is taken as proof that it is sahih, even without an explicit statement of authentication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this rule, if a ruling is found in all the authoritative matun but a contrary view appears in a commentary without explicit authentication, which should a mufti follow?
A) The view in the commentary because it is more detailed.
B) The ruling in the matun because it is implicitly authenticated.
C) The weakest opinion to be cautious.
D) The later opinion of the mashayikh regardless.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa is given based on the implicit authentication of the authoritative mutun unless a contrary view is explicitly authenticated.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Implicit Correction of Rulings in Authoritative Matn Books
Establishing the hierarchy of fatwa sources and the principle of implicit correction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three-tier hierarchy of sources for fatwa (mutun, shuruh, fatawa) and evaluate which ruling is mufta bih when disagreement exists.

Core Idea
A ruling in the authoritative matn is implicitly correct — it must be followed unless explicit correction comes from outside.

This passage from a rasm al-mufti text lays down the foundational hierarchy for issuing fatwa in the Hanafi school. It establishes that the presence of a ruling in the major matn books gives it implicit authority; commentaries and later fatwas are secondary. The principle of dimni tashih (implicit correction) ensures that fatwa is based on the most reliable layer of the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in question
When a mufti is asked about a case, first determine the specific ruling (hukm) that is contested or sought.
E.g., 'Is the testimony of a blind person valid?'
2
Check the authoritative matn books
Open standard matn works like Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, Multaqa al-Abhar. If the ruling is explicitly stated there, it is implicitly correct (mufta bih).
If found, proceed to step 3. If not, go to step 4.
3
Apply implicit correction unless explicit override exists
The matn's inclusion implies authenticity. However, if an explicit correction (tashih sarih) from a reliable authority outside the matn is found, that overrides. Otherwise, adopt the matn ruling.
Explicit correction must be clear and from an authoritative source.
4
If not in matn, move to commentaries (shuruh)
Check major commentaries like al-Hidayah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. If a ruling is mentioned there (and not in matn), it takes second priority.
Commentaries often expand on matn rulings.
5
If not in shuruh, consult fatwa collections (fatawa)
Finally, look into later fatwa compilations (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya). If no matn or commentary ruling exists, these provide guidance.
This is the lowest tier.

Source Text

کسی قول کا متون میں ہونا ، اس کی ضمنی تصحیح ہے
(۹) اس شعر میں علامہ شامی فرمارہے ہیں کہ جو قول متن کی معتبر کتابوں میں موجود ہو ، فتویٰ اسی پر دیا جائے گا ؛ اس لیے کہ کسی قول کا متونِ معتبرہ مثلاً :
بداية المبتدي، مختصر القدوري ، النقاية، وقاية، كنز الدقائق، ملتقى الأبحر“ وغیرہ کتابوں میں آجانا ، یہ اس قول کی ضمنی والتزامی تصحیح ہے، ان کتابوں کے مصنفین نے خاص طور پر صیح اقوال نقل کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے لہذا جو قول متونِ معتبرہ سے باہر ہوں گے، متون غیر معتبرہ میں، شروحات میں ، فتاویٰ میں؟ اُن پر فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ ہاں! اگر متون معتبرہ کے علاوہ قول کی صراحاً تصحیح وارد ہو، تو پھر ایسی صورت میں اسی پر فتوی دیا جائے گا؛ کیوں کہ صریح تصحیح التزامی صحیح پر رائج ہوتی ہے۔
مثال کے طور پر مذہب کے سبھی متون متفق ہیں کہ نا بینا شخص کی گواہی پر فیصلہ نہیں کیا جائے گا، جب کہ شروحات وغیرہ میں امام صاحب کی ایک روایت امام زفر کے واسطے سے، یقل کی گئی ہے کہ جن معاملات کا تعلق محض سماع سے : ہے اور اُن میں آنکھوں سے مشاہدے کی ضرورت نہیں، اُن میں نابینا کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی ، شروح کی یہ روایت متون کے خلاف ہے اور اس پر مشایخ کے فتوے کی صراحت بھی نہیں ہے؛ لہذا اُصولاً متون کی روایت پر فتویٰ دیا جائے گا اور یہ کہا جائے گا کہ نا بینا کی گواہی معتبر نہیں۔ خلاصہ کلام ! جس قول پر متون متفق ہوں، وہی مفتی بہ اور معتمد علیہ ہوگا، اُس کے بعد دوسرا نمبر اُن اقوال کا ہو گا، جو شروحات میں مذکور ہوں گے، تیسرا نمبر مشائخ کے فتاویٰ کا ہوگا، جب متون و شروحات میں کوئی روایت منقول نہ ہو، تو ایسی صورت میں فتاویٰ سے تائید حاصل کی جائے گی۔
The presence of a statement in the authoritative texts is its implicit correction. (9) In this verse, Allamah Shami says: That statement which is present in the reliable books of matn, fatwa will be given by it; because the presence of a statement in the authoritative matn books, for example: Bidayat al-Mubtadi, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Nuqayah, Wiqayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, Multaqa al-Abhar, etc., this is its implicit and necessary correction. The authors of these books have specifically committed to transmitting correct statements. Therefore, statements that are outside the authoritative matn books—in non-authoritative matn books, commentaries, fatwa collections—will not be given fatwa by them. Yes! If an explicit correction of a statement is reported from outside the authoritative matn, then in such case fatwa will be given by it; because explicit correction overrides the necessary correction. For example, all the matns of the madhhab agree that the testimony of a blind person will not be accepted. While in commentaries etc., a narration of Imam Abu Hanifa via Imam Zufar is transmitted that in matters that are purely auditory and do not require visual observation, the testimony of a blind person is acceptable. This narration from the commentaries is contrary to the matns, and there is no explicit fatwa of the mashayikh on it; therefore, in principle, fatwa will be given by the matn narration, and it will be said that the testimony of a blind person is not valid. Conclusion: The statement on which the matns are unanimous, that is the mufta bih and mu'tamad. After that, the second rank is for those statements that are mentioned in commentaries. The third rank is for the fatwas of the mashayikh. When no narration is transmitted in matns and commentaries, then in that situation support is sought from fatwas.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm al-mufti rule: the presence of a statement in the authoritative matn books serves as implicit correction (tashih dimni) of that statement. The rule is that any ruling found in the standard matn works (like Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, Multaqa al-Abhar, etc.) is considered implicitly authenticated because their authors undertook to transmit only correct opinions. If there is an explicit correction from outside the matn, it can override this implicit correction, but the default is to follow the matn. The passage gives an example: all matns agree that a blind person's testimony is inadmissible. A contrary narration via Imam Zufar appears in commentaries, but because no explicit fatwa from the mashayikh supports it, the matn ruling is followed. The passage concludes with a three-tier hierarchy for fatwa: first, the consensus of matns; second, opinions in commentaries; third, opinions in later fatwa collections. This hierarchy ensures that rulings are sourced from the most authoritative layers of the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
متون (mutun): The authoritative primary texts of the Hanafi madhhab, such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Kanz al-Daqa'iq
ضمنی تصحیح (dimni tashih): Implicit correction: the assumption that a ruling is correct because it is included in the authoritative matn books
مفتی بہ (mufta bih): The relied-upon ruling on which fatwa is given

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy established in this passage, which source is given the highest priority for issuing fatwa?
A) Commentaries (shuruh)
B) Fatwa collections (fatawa)
C) Authoritative matn books
D) The opinion of any later scholar

Key Takeaway
The authoritative matn books are the primary source for fatwa because their authors committed to transmitting only correct rulings, and their consensus constitutes implicit correction.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Identifying Rajih Opinion in Key Hanafi Works
Four verses setting out rasm al-mufti rules for preferred opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rules for identifying the rajih opinion in Hanafi texts: in Fatawa Qadikhan and Multaqa al-Abhar, the first-mentioned opinion is preferred; in other works (e.g., al-Hidayah), the later-mentioned opinion is relied upon, and apply them to determine the mufta bih.

Core Idea
In Fatawa Qadikhan and Multaqa, the first opinion is rajih; elsewhere, the later opinion is mufta bih.

This lesson introduces a key rasm al-mufti rule, often memorized in poetic form, that guides a mufti in selecting the correct fatwa from authoritative Hanafi compilations. The rule distinguishes between two categories of texts based on the author's editorial convention. Understanding this rule prevents a common mistake: assuming the first-mentioned opinion is always preferred regardless of the book.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the two categories
Internalize that there are two groups: (A) Fatawa Qadikhan (al-Khaniyyah) and Multaqa al-Abhar; (B) all other Hanafi works (like al-Hidayah, etc.).
The verses explicitly name the two books in group A.
2
Apply the rule for group A
For group A, the first-mentioned opinion among multiple is the rajih (preferred) and mufta bih. The verse says 'sābiq al-aqwāl ... dhū maziyyah' – the preceding statements have distinction.
This is the opposite of the default convention in most books.
3
Apply the rule for group B
For group B, the later-mentioned opinion is the reliable one (mufta bih) because the author typically delays the stronger proof. The verse says 'wa fī siwāhumā iʿtimid mā akhkharū dalīlahu' – rely on that whose proof they delayed.
The reasoning is that the author's habit is to present the stronger proof later (muharrar).
4
Handle the case of a single proof
If only one opinion is accompanied by a proof while the other is mentioned without evidence, the one with the proof is rajih. The verse says 'wa ka-dhā idhā mā wāḥidan qad ʿallalū lahu wa taʿlīla siwāhu ahmaliū'.
This rule applies across all books.

فتاوى قاضي خان “اور ”مُلتقى الابحُر“ میں راجح قول کی علامت
(٥) وَسَابِقُ الْأَقْوَالِ فِي الْخَانِيَّهُ * وَمُلْتَقَى الْأَبْحُرِ ذُو مَزِيَّهُ ۵۴ وَفِي سِوَاهُمَا اعْتُمِدَ مَا أَخَرُوا * دَليْلَهُ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُحَرَّرُ ۵۵ كَمَا هُوَ الْعَادَةُ فِي الْهِدَايَهُ * وَنَحْوِهَا لِرَاجِحِ الدِّرَايَهُ ٥٦ وَكَذَا إِذَا مَا وَاحِدًا قَدْ عَلَّلُوا * لَهُ، وَتَعْلِيْلَ سِوَاهُ أَهْمَلُوا

ترجمه : [۵۳] فتاوى قاضي خان اور ملتقى الأبحر میں پہلے ذکر کردہ اقوال فضیلت والے ( راج) ہیں۔ [۵۴] ان دونوں کتابوں کے علاوہ دیگر کتابوں میں ) اُن اقوال کو (فتوے کے لیے ) قابل اعتماد سمجھا گیا ہے، جن کی دلیل کو اُس کے مصنف نے بعد میں ذکر کیا ہے؛ کیوں کہ وہی قول مفتی بہ ہے۔ [۵۵] جیسا کہ ”هداية “ وغیرہ میں صاحب کتاب کا یہی طرز ہے، دلیل کے راجح ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ [۵۶] اسی طرح ( راج ہوگا) وہ قول، جس کی دلیل کو صاحب کتاب ذکر کریں اور اُس کے علاوہ دوسرے قول کی دلیل ذکر نہ کریں۔
شرح : ان چار اشعار میں علامہ شامی نے کتب فقہ میں مفتی بہ قول کی
The sign of the rajih opinion in Fatawa Qadikhan and Multaqa al-Abhar. (53) And the first of statements in al-Khaniyyah and Multaqa al-Abhar has distinction. (54) And in other than these two, rely upon that whose proof they delayed (i.e., mentioned later), because it is the authoritative (muharrar). (55) As is the habit in al-Hidayah and its likes, due to the proof being rajih. (56) And likewise, when they have given a proof for one (statement), and omitted the proof for the other. Translation: [53] In Fatawa Qadikhan and Multaqa al-Abhar, the statements mentioned first are superior (rajih). [54] In books other than these two, those statements are considered reliable (for fatwa) whose proof the author mentioned later, because that is the mufta bih. [55] As is the style in al-Hidayah etc., because the proof is rajih. [56] Similarly, (it is rajih) that statement for which the author mentioned a proof and did not mention a proof for the other. Commentary: In these four verses, Allamah Shami (has explained) the mufta bih opinion in fiqh books...
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm al-mufti rule in poetic form for identifying the rajih (preferred) opinion in different categories of Hanafi fiqh books. The four verses, from a longer poem, are explained in Urdu translation and commentary. The rule distinguishes between two categories: (1) In Fatawa Qadikhan and Multaqa al-Abhar, the first-mentioned opinion among multiple opinions is rajih. (2) In all other books (like al-Hidayah), the later-mentioned opinion is relied upon because the author typically delays the stronger proof. Additionally, if an author provides a proof for only one opinion, that opinion is considered rajih. This hierarchy helps muftis quickly determine which ruling to adopt based on the structure of the text they are consulting.

Key Terms
سابق الأقوال (sābiq al-aqwāl): The first-mentioned opinions in Fatawa Qadikhan and Multaqa al-Abhar
محرر (muḥarrar): The authoritative and relied-upon opinion
راجح الدراية (rājiḥ al-dirāyah): The stronger or preferred proof in terms of scholarly understanding

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) All commentaries
D) Only Fatawa Qadikhan

Key Takeaway
Knowing the text-specific ordering convention is essential for correctly identifying the mufta bih opinion in Hanafi works.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Identifying the Mufta Bih Opinion: Indicators in Key Hanafi Texts
Methodological rule for identifying mufta bih in Hanafi books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules from Rasm al-Mufti to identify the rajih (mufta bih) opinion in different types of Hanafi fiqh works.

Core Idea
The first-mentioned opinion in Fatawa Qazi Khan and Multaqa al-Abhur is rajih; in other works, the opinion with later proof is preferred.

In the Hanafi tradition, not every opinion recorded in a fiqh book carries equal weight for issuing fatwa. Later scholars, especially Allamah Shami, developed a system to identify the relied-upon (mufta bih) opinion. This lesson explains the indicators from the classic text 'Aqd Rasm al-Mufti,' differentiating between two categories of books.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two categories
Identify that the passage divides books into two groups: Fatawa Qazi Khan & Multaqa al-Abhur, and other works like al-Hidayah. Each group uses a different indicator for the rajih opinion.
This distinction is crucial for correct fatwa extraction.
2
Apply the first-method rule
For the first category, the opinion mentioned first in the discussion is the rajih (mufta bih). The author's order signals preference.
This rule applies specifically to Fatawa Qazi Khan and Multaqa al-Abhur.
3
Apply the second-method rule
For books like al-Hidayah and its commentaries, the opinion whose proof is given later (or the only one with proof) is the rajih. The delayed mention of evidence indicates the author's chosen view.
Also, if only one opinion has a proof, that is the rajih.
4
Understand the reasoning
These indicators work because authors order or prove based on strength. The method reflects the text's purpose: Fatawa Qazi Khan and Multaqa are fatwa compilations; al-Hidayah is a teaching text where proof is key.
The underlying principle is that the author's editorial choices reveal the preferred opinion.
5
Practice on a sample
Given a fictive page from a Hanafi book, identify the mufta bih using these rules. Determine which category the book falls into, then apply the correct indicator.
This step consolidates the skill.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي

(٥) وَسَابِقُ الْأَقْوَالِ فِي الْخَانِيَّهُ * وَمُلْتَقَى الْأَبْحُرِ ذُو مَزِيَّهُ ٥٤ وَفِي سِوَاهُمَا اعْتُمِدَ مَا أَخَرُوا * دَليْلَهُ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُحَرَّرُ ٥٥ كَمَا هُوَ الْعَادَةُ فِي الْهِدَايَهُ * وَنَحْوِهَا لِرَاجِحِ الدِّرَايَهُ ٥٦ وَكَذَا إِذَا مَا وَاحِدًا قَدْ عَلَّلُوا * لَهُ، وَتَعْلِيْلَ سِوَاهُ أَهْمَلُوا

ترجمه: [۵۳] فتاوى قاضي خان اور ملتقى الأبحر میں پہلے ذکر کردہ اقوال فضیلت والے (راجح) ہیں۔ [۵۴] ان دونوں کتابوں کے علاوہ دیگر کتابوں میں اُن اقوال کو (فتوے کے لیے) قابل اعتماد سمجھا گیا ہے، جن کی دلیل کو اُس کے مصنف نے بعد میں ذکر کیا ہے؛ کیوں کہ وہی قول مفتی بہ ہے۔ [۵۵] جیسا کہ ”هداية“ وغیرہ میں صاحب کتاب کا یہی طرز ہے، دلیل کے راجح ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ [۵۶] اسی طرح (راجح ہوگا) وہ قول، جس کی دلیل کو صاحب کتاب ذکر کریں اور اُس کے علاوہ دوسرے قول کی دلیل ذکر نہ کریں۔

شرح: ان چار اشعار میں علامہ شامی نے کتب فقہ میں مفتی بہ قول کی علامت و پہچان کو بیان فرمایا ہے، چناں چہ فرماتے ہیں کہ فتاوی قاضی خان اور ملتقى الأبحر میں راجح و مفتی بہ قول وہ ہوگا، جسے مصنف نے پہلے ذکر کیا ہو، گویا ان اقوال کا دیگر اقوال پر مقدم ہونا، ان کے رائج ہونے کی علامت ہے؟ لہذا ان کتابوں میں جو اقوال پہلے ذکر کیے گئے ہیں، اُن پر فتویٰ دیا جائے گا؟ کیوں کہ وہ راجح ہیں اور راجح قول کے مطابق فتوی دینا ضروری ہے۔

هداية" وغیرہ میں راجح قول کی علامت: علامہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مذکورہ دونوں کتابوں کے علاوہ دیگر فقہی کتابوں جیسے هداية، هداية كى شروحات كنز الدقائق کی شرحیں: مثلاً البحر الرائق تبيين الحقائق، اسی طرح بدائع الصنائع" وغیرہ میں راجح و مفتی بہ قول وہ ہوتا ہے، جس کی دلیل مصنف کتاب بعد میں ذکر کرتے ہیں، یعنی ان کتابوں میں کسی قول کی دلیل کا اخیر میں ذکر کیا جانا، اس کے مفتی بہ قول ہونے کی علامت و پہچان ہے۔

اِسی طرح مفتی بہ وراجح قول کی ایک علامت یہ ہے کہ فقہاء مختلف اقوال ذکر کریں مگر اُن میں سے کسی ایک ہی کی دلیل ذکر کریں، باقی اقوال کی دلیل ذکر نہ کریں، اُن کو بغیر دلیل ہی چھوڑ دیں؛ لہذا جس قول کی دلیل ذکر کی گئی ہے، وہ راج سمجھا جائے گا؟ اس لیے کہ یہ دلیل و علت کا ذکر اُس قول کے اہم ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔

ملاحظة: مذکورہ بالا تفصیل اس وقت ہے، جب کہ اس التزامی تصحیح نامور بالی تفصیل جب کہ اس ای کے مقابلے میں صراحۃ صحیح نہ پائی جائے۔
And the precedent of statements in al-Khaniyyah (Fatawa Qazi Khan) and Multaqa al-Abhur has merit (54). And in others, rely on what they delayed its proof, for it is the corrected (ruling) (55). As is the custom in al-Hidayah and its like, due to the preponderant understanding (56). And likewise, when they give a proof for one (statement) and neglect giving proof for another. Translation: [53] In Fatawa Qazi Khan and Multaqa al-Abhur, the statements mentioned first are the virtuous (rajih). [54] In books other than these two, those statements are considered reliable (for fatwa) whose proof the author mentioned later, because that is the mufta bih statement. [55] As is the custom in al-Hidayah etc., due to the proof being preponderant. [56] Similarly, the statement whose proof the author mentions while omitting the proof of other statements is rajih. Commentary: In these four verses, Allamah Shami explained the sign and recognition of the mufta bih statement in fiqh books. He says that in Fatawa Qazi Khan and Multaqa al-Abhur, the rajih and mufta bih statement is the one the author mentions first; its precedence over others indicates its prevalence. Therefore, in these books, fatwa is given according to statements mentioned first because they are rajih and fatwa must be according to the rajih. The sign of the rajih statement in al-Hidayah etc.: Allamah says that in other fiqh books besides these two, such as al-Hidayah, its commentaries, commentaries of Kanz al-Daqa'iq like al-Bahr al-Raiq and Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and also Bada'i' al-Sana'i', the rajih and mufta bih statement is the one whose proof the author mentions later; i.e., mentioning the proof at the end is the sign of its being mufta bih. Similarly, another sign is that when jurists mention multiple statements but give proof for only one of them, leaving others without proof, the statement with proof is considered rajih, because mentioning the proof indicates its importance.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) from Allamah Shami's commentary on Rasm al-Mufti. It identifies how to recognize the relied-upon (mufta bih) ruling in different types of Hanafi fiqh works. The author presents a poetic couplet and then explains it in Urdu. The rule distinguishes between two categories of books: those like Fatawa Qazi Khan and Multaqa al-Abhur, where the first mentioned opinion is rajih; and other books like al-Hidayah and its commentaries, where the opinion whose proof is given later (or the only one with proof) is rajih. This is crucial for a mufti to know which opinion to give fatwa upon when multiple opinions exist in a text. The reasoning given is that the order of mention or the presence of proof indicates the strength of the opinion. The sharh elaborates that in Fatawa Qazi Khan and Multaqa, the first opinion is preferred because it is the more prevalent one; in other books, later mention of proof suggests it is the corrected version, and exclusive mention of proof highlights the author's choice.

Key Terms
راجح (rajih): The preponderant opinion that should be followed in fatwa.
مفتی بہ (mufta bih): The ruling upon which fatwa is given; the relied-upon position.
فتاوی قاضی خان (Fatawa Qazi Khan): A famous collection of Hanafi fatawa by Qazi Khan (d. 592/1196).
ملتقى الأبحر (Multaqa al-Abhur): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh manual by Ibrahim al-Halabi (d. 956/1549).
هداية (al-Hidayah): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by al-Marghinani (d. 593/1197).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In al-Hidayah, how does one identify the rajih (mufta bih) opinion according to this passage?
A) The opinion mentioned first.
B) The opinion whose proof is mentioned later or which is the only one with a proof.
C) The opinion found in Fatawa Qazi Khan.
D) The opinion that appears in the middle of a discussion.

Key Takeaway
The indicator for the relied-upon opinion varies by text: first mention in Fatawa Qazi Khan and Multaqa al-Abhur, later proof in al-Hidayah and similar works.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

Signs of the Preferred Opinion in Hanafi Fiqh Books
Explaining signs to identify the preferred opinion in Hanafi fiqh books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the signs of the preferred opinion (rajih/mufta bih) in different Hanafi fiqh books and apply the hierarchy between implicit signs and explicit corrections.

Core Idea
Preferred opinion is identified by author's order or proof placement; explicit corrections override all implicit signs.

This lesson from 'Aun al-Mughni' equips you with the methodological tools to locate the relied-upon (mufta bih) opinion within Hanafi texts. You will learn the key signs—such as which opinion is mentioned first or whose proof is given last—and understand when an explicit correction (tasreeh sahih) takes precedence. Mastering these signs is essential for sound fatwa and scholarly research.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between book categories
Identify whether the book belongs to the group where the first-mentioned opinion is rajih (e.g., Fatawa Qadi Khan, Multaqa al-Abhar) or the group where the opinion whose proof is mentioned last is rajih (e.g., al-Hidayah, Bada'i al-Sana'i').
This distinction is critical because the sign differs by book.
2
Apply the sign of sole proof
If the author presents multiple opinions but provides the proof (dalil) for only one, that opinion is preferred because the author's effort to cite evidence indicates its importance.
This sign applies when no explicit correction exists.
3
Check for explicit corrections
Look for phrases like 'al-fatwa alayh', 'al-sahih', 'al-ashbah', 'al-azhar', or 'al-mukhtar'. These tasreeh sahih explicitly state which opinion is correct.
Explicit corrections override all implicit signs (order, proof placement).
4
Apply the hierarchy
If an explicit correction is present, follow it directly. Otherwise, use the implicit signs appropriate to the book. Among explicit corrections, 'al-ashbah' and 'al-azhar' are stronger than others.
This hierarchy ensures consistency in fatwa.

Source Text

شیخ الاسلام حضرت مولانا مفتی محمد تقی عثمانی صاحب زید مسجد ہم فرماتے ہیں کہ صاحب ”بدائع الصنائع “ کے طرز عمل سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ اکثر و بیشتر راج قول کو پہلے ذکر کرتے ہیں۔
ويظهر من صنيع صاحب البدائع أنه يفعل ذلك أيضاً في الغالب.
أصول الإفتاء وآدابه : ۱۸۵)
تصحیح صریحی کے الفاظ
وَحَيْثُمَا وَجَدْتَ قَوْلَيْنِ، وَقَدْ * صُحِحَ وَاحِدٌ، فَذَاكَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ ۵۸ بنحو : ذَا الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ الْأَشْبَهُ * وَالأَظْهَرُ الْمُخْتَارُ ذَا وَالْأَوْجَهُ أوِ الصَّحِيحُ وَالأصَحُ، اكد * مِنهُ، وَقِيلَ: عَكْسُهُ الْمُؤكَّد كَذَا بِهِ يُفْتَى ، عَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى * وَذَانِ مِنْ جَمِيعِ تِلْكَ أَقْوى
He explained the sign and identification. Thus he says: In Fatawa Qadi Khan and Multaqa al-Abhar, the preferred and mufta bih opinion is the one that the author mentioned first; indeed, the precedence of these opinions over others is a sign of their prevalence. Therefore, in these books, fatwa will be given according to the opinions mentioned first, because they are preferred and it is necessary to give fatwa according to the preferred opinion. Second: The sign of the preferred opinion in Hidayah etc. The scholar says that besides the two mentioned books, in other fiqh books such as Hidayah, its commentaries, and commentaries on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, e.g., al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and similarly Bada'i al-Sana'i', the preferred and mufta bih opinion is the one whose proof the author mentions later. That is, in these books, mentioning the proof of an opinion at the end is a sign that it is the mufta bih opinion. Similarly, another sign of the mufta bih and preferred opinion is that the jurists mention various opinions but provide the proof for only one of them, leaving the others without proof. Therefore, the opinion for which the proof is given will be considered preferred, because the mention of its proof and rationale indicates its importance. Note: The above detail applies when there is no explicit correction (tasreeh sahih) against it. The opinion of Shaykh al-Islam. Shaykh al-Islam Mawlana Mufti Muhammad Taqi Uthmani says that from the practice of the author of Bada'i al-Sana'i', it appears that he usually mentions the preferred opinion first. And it appears from the practice of the author of Bada'i that he also does that in most cases. (Usul al-Ifta' wa Adabuh, p. 185) The words of explicit correction: And whenever you find two statements, and one has been corrected, that is the relied-upon. By such phrases as 'al-fatwa alayh', 'al-ashbah', 'al-azhar', 'al-mukhtar', 'al-awjahu', or 'al-sahih' and 'al-asahh'. It is said to be emphatic, and its opposite is the emphatic; thus fatwa is given by it. And these two are the strongest among all those.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage from 'Aun al-Mughni' outlines the methodological signs (qara'in) that a mufti uses to identify the preferred (rajih) and relied-upon (mufta bih) opinion within the Hanafi madhhab when a book does not explicitly state a preference. The author begins by explaining that in the works of Qadi Khan and Multaqa al-Abhar, the opinion mentioned first is the one to be given fatwa upon, as it indicates the author's preference. Then, for books like al-Hidayah and its commentaries (e.g., al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and Bada'i al-Sana'i'), the sign is reversed: the opinion whose proof is mentioned last is the preferred one. Additionally, if multiple opinions are presented but only one is accompanied by its proof, that opinion is taken as the rajih because the author's effort to provide evidence signals its importance. However, these implicit signs only apply when there is no explicit corrective phrase (tasreeh sahih) such as 'al-fatwa alayh' or 'al-sahih'. The passage then cites Shaykh al-Islam Mufti Muhammad Taqi Uthmani's observation that Imam al-Kasani in Bada'i often places the rajih opinion first, aligning with the first sign. Finally, a poetic summary explains that when two conflicting statements are found and one is explicitly corrected with terms like 'al-ashbah', 'al-azhar', or 'al-sahih', that is the authoritative view. This establishes a hierarchy: explicit correction overrides implicit signs, and among explicit corrections, some phrases like 'al-ashbah' and 'al-azhar' are stronger than others. The mufti must apply this hierarchy consistently.

Key Terms
راجح (rajih): The stronger or preferred opinion among multiple scholarly views, to be given precedence in fatwa.
مفتی بہ (mufta bih): The opinion upon which fatwa is given; the relied-upon view in the madhhab.
تصحیح صریحی (tasreeh sahih): An explicit corrective statement indicating a particular opinion is correct or preferred, such as 'al-fatwa alayh' or 'al-sahih'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In al-Hidayah, which opinion is considered raajih if no explicit correction is present?
A) The opinion mentioned first in the book
B) The opinion whose proof is mentioned last in the book
C) The opinion that is shorter in wording
D) The opinion that agrees with the Shafi'i school

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy for identifying the mufta bih opinion is: first, explicit corrections; then, implicit signs appropriate to the book (first-mentioned or proof-last); finally, other indicators like sole provision of proof.

The Hierarchy of Explicit Correction Phrases in Hanafi Fatwa Methodology
Explaining the hierarchy of explicit tasheeh phrases in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and rank the explicit correction phrases in Hanafi fatwa literature and apply the hierarchy to determine the mufta bihi ruling when conflicting corrections exist.

Core Idea
When two opinions exist, the explicitly corrected one is the mu'tamad, and among phrases, 'bihi yufta' and 'alayhi al-fatwa' are strongest.

In Hanafi fatwa practice, not all corrections are equal. This lesson unpacks the explicit correction (tasheeh sarihi) phrases used by Hanafi jurists, their relative strengths, and how to apply this hierarchy in determining the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting rulings
In a fiqh case, locate the differing opinions; note that one may have an explicit correction mark.
Explicit correction can appear in matn or commentary.
2
Find the correction phrase
Scan the text for any of the explicit correction phrases listed: al-fatwa alayh, al-ashbah, al-azhar, al-mukhtar, al-awjah, al-sahih, al-asahh, bihi yufta, alayhi al-fatwa, and others mentioned in the commentary.
3
Rank the phrase
Use the established hierarchy: weakest are al-ashbah, al-azhar, al-mukhtar, al-awjah; then al-sahih/al-asahh (with disagreement on which is stronger); strongest are bihi yufta and alayhi al-fatwa.
The passage notes that some hold 'asahh' stronger, others 'sahih'; this ikhtilaf is secondary if stronger phrases exist.
4
Apply the strongest correction
If multiple corrections exist, the opinion with the strongest phrase becomes the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).
If no correction phrase is found, implicit correction (tasheeh iltizami) indicators should be considered.

ويظهر من صنيع صاحب البدائع أنه يفعل ذلك أيضاً في الغالب.
أصول الإفتاء وآدابه : 185)
تصحیح صریحی کے الفاظ
وَحَيْثُمَا وَجَدْتَ قَوْلَيْنِ، وَقَدْ * صُحِحَ وَاحِدٌ، فَذَاكَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ ۵۸ بنحو : ذَا الْفَتْوَى عَلَيْهِ الْأَشْبَهُ * وَالأَظْهَرُ الْمُخْتَارُ ذَا وَالْأَوْجَهُ أوِ الصَّحِيحُ وَالأصَحُ، اكد * مِنهُ، وَقِيلَ: عَكْسُهُ الْمُؤكَّد كَذَا بِهِ يُفْتَى ، عَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى * وَذَانِ مِنْ جَمِيعِ تِلْكَ أَقْوى
