Classification of 'Urf: General vs. Specific Custom and Their Legal Authority
Defines 'urf 'amm and 'urf khaas with examples and rules for mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for when 'urf 'amm and 'urf khaas are valid in issuing fatwas.

Core Idea
Custom can only override a text by specification, not abandonment; only general custom may specify.

This passage from a rasm al-mufti work explains the two types of custom and the critical conditions a mufti must observe when relying on them. Understanding these distinctions prevents misuse of local practices that contradict clear textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish 'urf 'amm and 'urf khaas
Identify the defining features: prevalence (all countries vs. one city) and legal effect (general vs. specific ruling).
2
Learn the three-case rule regarding nass
Study the summary: if custom necessitates abandoning nass → invalid; if specifying nass → only 'urf 'amm; if neither → 'urf khaas valid.
3
Analyze the istisna' example
See how 'urf 'amm specifies the prohibition of selling non-existent items, permitting istisna' without fully abandoning the prohibition.
4
Analyze the oath example
Understand how 'urf khaas defines the meaning of 'food' in Bangalore so that an oath not to eat food is limited to rice.
5
Apply the rule to a new custom
Given a hypothetical local custom, evaluate its validity using the three-case framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عرف عام: ایسا رواج ، جو تمام ممالک میں رائج ہو۔ عرف خاص: ایسا معاملہ جو کسی خاص شہر میں رائج ہو ، پورے ملک میں نہ ہو۔ عرف عام سے عمومی حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے اور اُس کے ذریعے قیاس اور حدیث میں تخصیص کی جاتی ہے۔ عرف خاص کا معاملہ اس سے مختلف ہے؛ کیوں کہ اُس سے خاص حکم ثابت ہوتا ہے، بہ شرطے کہ وہ قیاس یا حدیث کے خلاف نہ ہو؛ کیوں کہ عرف خاص قیاس وحدیث کے لیے مختص نہیں بن سکتا۔ عرف عام کی مثال استصناع ( آرڈر دے کر طبیع تیار کرانا) کی بیچ، یہ عرف و تعامل کی وجہ سے جائز ہے، حالاں کہ یہ غیر موجود شی ء کی بیع ہے، جو شرعاً ممنوع ہے ، مگر جس نص میں بیع معدوم سے منع کیا گیا ہے، اس میں تخصیص کرتے ہوئے ، بر بنائے تعامل صرف استصناع کی بیچ کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے، اس کے علاوہ میں بیچ معدوم کی ” نہی اپنی جگہ پر یہ دستور قائم ہے؛ لہذا نص کو بالکلیہ ترک کرنا لازم نہیں آیا۔ ہاں! اگر استصناع کے علاوہ بھی خرید وفروخت کی تمام صورتوں میں مبیع کے معدوم ہوتے ہوئے بھیج کو جائز قرار دیا جائے ، تو یہ نص کو ترک کرنا ہوگا ، جو کہ کسی بھی طرح درست نہیں۔ عرف خاص سے اگر ترک نص یا تخصیص نص لازم نہ آئے ، تو عرف خاص اس کے استعمال کرنے والوں میں ایمان (قسموں کے بارے ) میں متعارف الفاظ، اسی طرح بیچ را جارہ وغیرہ میں رائج طور طریقے میں معتبر ہوتا ہے؛ اگر چہ وہ عرف ظاهر الرواية “ کے خلاف ہو۔ عرف خاص کی مثال بنگلور وغیرہ سمیت جنوبی ہند کے متعدد شہروں میں کھانا " چاول کو کہا جاتا ہے، دیگر بہت سے علاقوں میں مطلقا کھانے کی چیز خواہ روٹی ہو یا چاول ، سب پر کھانے کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے؛ لہذا بنگلور کا رہنے والا شخص اگر یہ قسم کھانے کہ میں کھانا نہیں کھاؤں گا، پھر وہ روٹی کھالے، تو حانث نہیں ہوگا؛ کیوں کہ اس کی قسم کے الفاظ کا اعتبار اُن کے عرف کے مطابق ہوگا اور یہ سمجھا جائے گا کہ اُس نے خاص طور پر چاول نہ کھانے کی قسم کھائی ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام . عرف کی وجہ سے اگر ترک نص لازم آتا ہو ، تو مطلقا عرف کا اعتبار نہیں، خواہ عرف عام ہو یا خاص۔ . عرف کی وجہ سے اگر نص میں تخصیص لازم آرہی ہو، تو ایسی صورت میں صرف عرف عام کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ اگر عرف کے مطابق عمل کرنے سے نہ ترک نص لازم آتا ہو، نہ تخصیص نص تو ایسی صورت میں عرف خاص بھی معتبر ہے۔
General custom: a custom prevalent in all countries. Specific custom: a practice prevalent in a particular city, not the whole country. General custom establishes a general ruling and through it, specification (takhsis) is made in qiyas and hadith. The case of specific custom is different from this; because it establishes a specific ruling, on condition that it is not contrary to qiyas or hadith; because specific custom cannot become a specifier for qiyas and hadith. Example of general custom: the sale of istisna' (ordering a product to be made). This is permissible due to custom and mutual dealing, although it is the sale of a non-existent thing, which is prohibited by shari'a. However, by specifying the text which prohibited the sale of a non-existent thing, on the basis of dealing, only the sale of istisna' is deemed permissible. Apart from this, the prohibition of selling a non-existent thing remains in place; thus it was not necessary to abandon the text entirely. Yes! If in all cases of buying and selling, the sale of a non-existent object is permissible, then that would be abandoning the text, which is not correct in any way. If from specific custom neither abandonment (tark) of the text nor specification (takhsis) of the text follows, then specific custom is valid among those who use it, in the customary words regarding oaths, as well as in the prevalent methods of sale, etc., even if it is contrary to the custom in Zahir al-Riwaya. Example of specific custom: In Bangalore and various cities of South India, 'food' is called rice. In many other regions, 'food' applies absolutely to any edible item, whether bread or rice. Therefore, if a person from Bangalore swears an oath saying 'I will not eat food,' and then he eats bread, he is not guilty of breaking the oath; because the words of his oath are considered according to their custom, and it will be understood that he specifically swore not to eat rice. Summary: If due to custom, abandonment of the text (tark nass) becomes necessary, then custom is absolutely not valid, whether general or specific. If due to custom, specification of the text (takhsis nass) becomes necessary, then in that case only general custom is valid. If acting according to custom does not lead to abandonment of the text nor specification of the text, then in that case specific custom is also valid.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule concerning the types of 'urf (custom) and when a mufti may rely on them. The text first defines 'urf 'amm (general custom) as a practice prevalent in all countries, and 'urf khaas (specific custom) as a practice limited to a particular city or region. It explains that 'urf 'amm can specify general rulings derived from qiyas or hadith, while 'urf khaas cannot specify those sources but may establish a specific ruling only if it does not contradict qiyas or hadith. The author provides two examples: for 'urf 'amm, the istisna' contract (order to manufacture), which is permitted despite the general prohibition of selling non-existent items, because the custom of people is taken into account. For 'urf khaas, the example of the word 'food' in Bangalore, where it specifically means rice, so an oath not to eat 'food' is understood according to that custom. The summary clarifies the hierarchy: if a custom leads to abandoning a clear text (tark nass), it is invalid regardless of being general or specific. If it leads to specifying (takhsis) a text, only general custom is valid. If it does neither, then specific custom may also be considered valid. This rule guides the mufti in weighing custom against revealed sources.

Key Terms
عرف عام ('urf 'amm): A custom prevalent in all countries, which can specify general texts and establish a general ruling.
عرف خاص ('urf khaas): A practice limited to a particular city or group, valid only if it does not oppose qiyas/hadith and does not lead to tark nass or takhsis nass.
استصناع (istisna'): A contract for ordering a manufactured good, allowed by custom despite selling a non-existent item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is 'urf khaas (specific custom) considered valid?
A) When it opposes qiyas but not nass
B) When it does not necessitate abandoning or specifying nass
C) When it is accompanied by ijma'
D) When it is widespread in all regions

Key Takeaway
The validity of custom depends on its effect on the nass: abandonment invalid, specification only for general custom, and if no conflict, specific custom may be valid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Weak Opinions in Fatwa and Qada: Rule and Exceptions
Ruling on weak opinions with two exceptions and an example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule regarding weak opinions in Hanafi fatwa and qada, and identify the two exceptional circumstances where a weak opinion may be followed.

Core Idea
Weak opinions are not allowed for fatwa or qada, except in cases of dire necessity or when a highly expert mufti deems them strong.

In the Hanafi madhhab, the preferred (rajih) opinion is the standard for fatwa and judicial decisions. But what if a weak (da'if) opinion offers relief in hardship? This lesson from 'Aun al-Mughni' unpacks the strict rule and its two carefully defined exceptions, illustrating with a classic ghusl example.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Identify the baseline: a mufti cannot act upon or give fatwa based on a weak opinion, nor can a qadi use it in judgment.
The rule is established by consensus (ijma).
2
Identify the first exception
A person in dire necessity (‘umum al-balwa) may follow a weak opinion if no other option exists.
Necessity is determined by the mufti or by the individual’s genuine hardship.
3
Analyze the ghusl example
The example shows how necessity (travel, embarrassment) allows following Imam Abu Yusuf’s weak opinion instead of the rajih view of Abu Hanifa.
The weak opinion becomes mufta bih temporarily due to hardship.
4
Identify the second exception
A mufti with deep juristic expertise may adopt a weak opinion if he independently considers it strong based on other evidence.
This requires ijtihad-level skill, not ordinary knowledge.
5
Distinguish the rule for qadis
Judges are strictly bound to the rajih opinion; any verdict based on a weak opinion is null and void.
Modern qadis are explicitly restricted by appointment terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَاسِيَّمَا قُضَاتُنَا إِذْ قُيّدُوا * بِرَاجِحِ الْمَذْهَبِ حِيْنَ فَلِدُوا وَلَمْ مَا نَظَمُتُهُ فِي سِلْك * وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ عِمَامُ مِسْكِ

ترجمہ: (۷۰) ضعیف قول پر مفتی نہ خود عمل کر سکتا ہے اور نہ ہی کسی مسئلہ معلوم کرنے کے لیے آنے والے سائل کو، اُس کے مطابق فتوی دے سکتا ہے۔ [۲۱] ہاں ! اگر کوئی ایسا شخص ہو، جسے کوئی سخت ضرورت در پیش ہو یا خود مفتی ایسا ہو کہ جسے خوب فقہی مہارت حاصل ہو ( تو ایسے دو شخص ضعیف قول پر عمل کر سکتے ہیں)۔ ۷۲ لیکن قاضی ( بہ ہر حال ) ضعیف قول کے مطابق فیصلہ نہیں کر سکتا اور اگر (بالفرض) کر بھی دیا تو اس کا یہ فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہو گا۔ [۷۳] خاص طور پر ہمارے زمانے کے قاضی ( کا فیصلہ نافذ ہوگا ہی نہیں ) ؛ اس لیے کہ انھیں عہدہ قضا پر فائز کرتے وقت ، مذہب کے راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنے کا پابند کر دیا گیا ہے۔ [۷۴] ( فتویٰ نویسی کے ) جن اصول وضوابط کو میں ( اشعار کی ) لڑی میں پرور ہاتھا، وہ مکمل ہو گئے اور الحمد للہ مشک کی مہر ہے۔ شرح : علامہ شامی بالکل شروع میں یہ بات بیان فرما چکے ہیں کہ بالا جماع راجح قول کی پیروی لازم وضروری ہے، اس کے خلاف مرجوح اور ضعیف قول پر فتویٰ دینا جائز نہیں ، اب یہاں سے حضرت علامہ صلى الله عليه وسلم بعض ایسی صورتیں ذکر کرنا چاہتے ہیں، جن میں قول ضعیف پر عمل جائز ہے مگر اصل راجح قول پر ہی عمل کرنا ہے؛ اس لیے پہلے یہاں بھی اصل ہونے کے اعتبار سے مکرراُس کا تذکرہ کر دیا، اس کے بعد فرماتے ہیں کہ دو صورتوں میں ضعیف قول پر فتوی دینے اور عمل کرنے کی گنجائش ہے۔

پہلی صورت: ایک شخص بہت زیادہ ضرورت مند ہے، اُسے اپنی کسی مجبوری کی وجہ سے ضعیف قول کو اختیار کیے بغیر کوئی چارہ نہیں تو ایسا مجبور شخص ضعیف قول پر عمل کر سکتا ہے۔ جیسے : حنفیہ کے یہاں حضرات طرفین کے نزدیک وجوب غسل کے لیے اتنا کافی ہے کہ منی اپنی جگہ سے شہوت کے ساتھ ہٹ جائے ، شرم گاہ سے باہر آتے ہوئے شہوت ہو یا نہ ہوا یہی مطلقی بہ قول ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ وجوب غسل کے لیے منی کا شرم گاہ سے شہوت کے ساتھ لکھنا ضروری ہے، یہ ضعیف قول ہے ، لیکن اگر کوئی مسافر ایسی جگہ یا ایسی سواری میں سفر میں ہو ، جہاں اُسے سفر میں غسل کرنے میں پریشانی ہو یا کسی جگہ مہمان ہو اور غسل جنابت کرنے میں اُسے شرم آتی ہو اور اُس پر تہمت لگنے کا اندیشہ ہو، تو حضرات فقہاء نے ایسے شخص کو اجازت دی ہے کہ اگر وہ انزال کے وقت عضو مخصوص کو پکڑلے اور منی نہ نکلنے دے، پھر جب شہوت ختم ہو جائے ، تب منی کا خروج ہوا تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق اس پر غسل کرنا ضروری نہیں ہوگا ، امام ابو یوسف کا یہ قول مفتی بہ نہیں ، مگر ضرورت کی وجہ سے اسے مفتی بہ بنا دیا گیا۔

دوسری صورت: کوئی مفتی اگر ڈی رائے ، بالغ نظر اتنی مضبوط صلاحیت کا مالک ہو کہ وہ فقہاء کے ضعیف قول کو، دوسری کسی دلیل کی بنیاد پر قوی سمجھے، تو پھر ایسی صورت میں وہ فقہاء کے ضعیف قول پر عمل کر سکتا ہے۔
Especially our judges, since they are restricted, with the preferred opinion of the madhhab when they were born. And whatever I have composed in a string, and praise be to Allah, it is a crown of musk.

Translation: (70) A mufti cannot himself act upon a weak opinion, nor can he give a fatwa according to it to a questioner who comes to find out a ruling. Yes! If there is a person who is facing a severe necessity, or the mufti himself is such that he has deep juristic expertise (then such two persons can act upon a weak opinion). 72 But a judge (in any case) cannot decide by a weak opinion, and if (hypothetically) he does so, his verdict will not be effective. [73] Especially the judges of our time (their verdict will not be effective); because at the time of their appointment they were bound to decide according to the preferred opinion of the madhhab. [74] The principles and regulations of fatwa writing that I have strung in a poetic line are complete, and praise be to Allah, it is a seal of musk. Commentary: Allama Shami stated at the very beginning that it is necessary and obligatory to follow the preferred opinion by consensus; it is not permissible to give fatwa according to a weaker or weak opinion. Now here the respected author (peace be upon him) wants to mention some situations in which acting upon a weak opinion is permissible, but the original principle is to act upon the preferred opinion. Therefore he first repeated that here as well, then says that in two situations there is scope for giving fatwa and acting upon a weak opinion.

First situation: A person is in dire need; he has no choice except to adopt the weak opinion due to some compulsion, so such a compelled person can act upon the weak opinion. For example: In the Hanafi school, according to the two masters, for the obligation of ghusl, it is sufficient that the semen moves from its place with desire; whether desire remains or not during exit—this is the absolute preferred opinion. Imam Abu Yusuf says that for the obligation of ghusl, it is necessary that the semen exits from the private part with desire; this is a weak opinion. But if a traveler is in a place or in a vehicle where he faces difficulty in performing ghusl, or he is a guest and feels shy to perform ghusl of janabah, and he fears being accused, then the jurists have permitted such a person to hold his specific organ at the time of ejaculation and not let the semen come out; then when the desire subsides, when the semen exits, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, ghusl will not be obligatory upon him. Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is not mufta bih (relied upon for fatwa), but due to necessity it was made mufta bih.

Second situation: If a mufti is of deep thought, far-sighted, and possesses such strong ability that he considers the weak opinion of the jurists to be strong based on some other evidence, then in such a case he can act upon the weak opinion.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule from the work 'Aun al-Mughni', which is a commentary on 'Rasm al-Mufti' by Ibn Abidin. It addresses the critical question: when can a weak (da'if) opinion in the Hanafi madhhab be used for fatwa or qada? The general principle is that only the preferred (rajih) opinion is permissible for fatwa and judicial decisions, and this is established by consensus. The author then refines this rule by presenting two exceptions specifically for fatwa (not for qada): first, a person in extreme necessity who has no alternative but to follow a weak opinion; second, a mufti who possesses deep juristic expertise and, based on his own reasoning, considers the weak opinion to be strong due to another evidence. For qadis, the rule is absolute: a judge cannot base his verdict on a weak opinion, and any such verdict is null and void, especially as modern judges are explicitly bound to the rajih opinion upon appointment.

The commentary by Allama Shami reinforces that the author repeats the general rule before mentioning the exceptions. The first exception is illustrated with a fiqh example from the obligations of ghusl. The dominant Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that ghusl becomes obligatory merely by the movement of semen from its place with desire, even if it exits without desire. The weak opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf requires the actual exit with desire for ghusl to be obligatory. Normally, fatwa is given on the preferred opinion, but in situations where performing ghusl is extremely difficult—such as for a traveler or a guest who fears embarrassment or accusation—the jurists allowed acting upon Abu Yusuf's opinion. This is a concession (rukhsa) rather than the general ruling. The second exception allows a highly skilled mufti, who can perform independent tarjih (preference) based on evidence, to consider a normally weak opinion as strong and act upon it. This preserves the integrity of the madhhab while allowing adaptation in exceptional cases.

Key Terms
قول ضعیف (qawl da'if): A weak opinion within the Hanafi madhhab that is not relied upon for fatwa or qada generally
راجح (rajih): The preferred opinion in the madhhab, which is the basis for fatwa and judicial decisions
مفتی بہ (mufta bih): The opinion that is relied upon for issuing fatwas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If the weak opinion is more merciful
B) If the qadi has deep expertise
C) Never; any such verdict is invalid
D) If the litigants agree

Key Takeaway
The general rule is strict: weak opinions are not allowed for fatwa or qada, but necessity and mufti expertise create limited, carefully defined exceptions.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

When Can Weak Opinions Be Used in Fatwa and Judgment?
Explains when weak opinions can be used in fatwa and judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions that permit using weak opinions in fatwa and distinguish the rules for mufti and qadi regarding weak opinions.

Core Idea
Weak opinions permitted in fatwa under necessity or mufti's strong conviction; in judgment, only a mujtahid qadi can enforce them.

In Hanafi usul al-ifta, the default is to act on the preponderant (rajih) opinion. However, there are exceptional circumstances where a weak opinion may be given as a fatwa or even used in a court judgment. This lesson, drawn from 'Aun al-Mughni' on Rasm al-Mufti, clarifies those conditions and the critical distinction between fatwa and qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios for weak opinions in fatwa
The text presents two situations: extreme necessity (the person has no other option) and the mufti's own strong reasoning (he considers the weak opinion stronger based on other evidence). Identify each scenario as distinct.
These are exceptions, not the rule.
2
Understand the ghusl example
The relied-upon Hanafi view: ghusl becomes wajib when semen moves from its place with desire. Imam Abu Yusuf's weak view requires actual exit with desire. The text shows how necessity permits adopting Abu Yusuf's view for a traveler facing difficulty.
This example illustrates the necessity condition.
3
Distinguish the rule for mufti vs. qadi
The author states that the permission for weak opinions is limited to fatwa. In judgment (qada), the general rule is that the qadi must decide by the preponderant opinion.
Mufti can give fatwa by weak opinion under conditions; qadi cannot.
4
Differentiate between mujtahid and muqallid qadi
If a mujtahid qadi decides by a weak opinion, his decision is enforceable because his ijtihad strengthens it. If a muqallid qadi does so, his decision is void because he is bound by the preponderant opinion of the madhhab.
The key factor is the qadi's level of ijtihad.

Source Text

عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي
کر دیا، اس کے بعد فرماتے ہیں کہ دو صورتوں میں ضعیف قول پر فتوی دینے اور عمل کرنے کی گنجائش ہے۔
پہلی صورت
ایک شخص بہت زیادہ ضرورت مند ہے، اُسے اپنی کسی مجبوری کی وجہ سے ضعیف قول کو اختیار کیے بغیر کوئی چارہ نہیں تو ایسا مجبور شخص ضعیف قول پر عمل کر سکتا ہے۔ جیسے : حنفیہ کے یہاں حضرات طرفین کے نزدیک وجوب غسل کے لیے اتنا کافی ہے کہ منی اپنی جگہ سے شہوت کے ساتھ ہٹ جائے ، شرم گاہ سے باہر آتے ہوئے شہوت ہو یا نہ ہوا یہی مطلقی بہ قول ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ وجوب غسل کے لیے منی کا شرم گاہ سے شہوت کے ساتھ لکھنا ضروری ہے، یہ ضعیف قول ہے ، لیکن اگر کوئی مسافر ایسی جگہ یا ایسی سواری میں سفر میں ہو ، جہاں اُسے سفر میں غسل کرنے میں پریشانی ہو یا کسی جگہ مہمان ہو اور غسل جنابت کرنے میں اُسے شرم آتی ہو اور اُس پر تہمت لگنے کا اندیشہ ہو، تو حضرات فقہاء نے ایسے شخص کو اجازت دی ہے کہ اگر وہ انزال کے وقت عضو مخصوص کو پکڑلے اور منی نہ نکلنے دے، پھر جب شہوت ختم ہو جائے ، تب منی کا خروج ہوا تو حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے قول کے مطابق اس پر غسل کرنا ضروری نہیں ہوگا ، امام ابو یوسف کا یہ قول مفتی بہ نہیں ، مگر ضرورت کی وجہ سے اسے مفتی بہ بنا دیا گیا۔
دوسری صورت
کوئی مفتی اگر ڈی رائے ، بالغ نظر اتنی مضبوط صلاحیت کا مالک ہو کہ وہ فقہاء کے ضعیف قول کو، دوسری کسی دلیل کی بنیاد پر قوی سمجھے، تو پھر ایسی صورت میں وہ فقہاء کے ضعیف قول پر عمل کر سکتا ہے۔

عون المغني في حل عقود رسم المفتي
حاصل کلام
۱۰۹
مجبوری کے درجے میں ضعیف قول پر مفتی خود بھی عمل کر سکتا ہے، دوسروں کو بھی فتوی دے سکتا ہے، احناف کا صحیح قول اس سلسلے میں یہی ہے۔
قولِ ضعیف پر فیصلہ کرنا مطلقاً درست نہیں
رہی بات قاضی کی کہ وہ ضعیف قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟ تو اس سلسلے میں علامہ شامی صلى الله عليه وسلم فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ اجازت صرف فتوے کی حد تک ہے، جہاں تک قضا و فیصلے کی بات ہے، تو اس میں ضعیف قول پر عمل درست نہیں ۔ قاضی اگر مجتہد ہے، تو اُس پر لازم ہے کہ وہ اس قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرے، جو اُس کے نزدیک راجح ہے اور اگر قاضی مقلد ہے، تو اُس پر مذہب کے راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنا لازم ہے؛ کیوں کہ اُنھیں عہدہ قضاء سپر د کیے جانے کے وقت ، مذہب کے راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنے کا پابند کر دیا گیا ہے؛ لہذا دونوں طرح کے قاضی پر ہر حال میں راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنا لازم ہے؛ البتہ قاضی مجتہد نے اگر قولِ ضعیف کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دیا، تو وہ نافذ ہو جائے گا ؛ اس لیے کہ ضعیف قول قاضی مجتہد کے فیصلے سے قوی ہو جاتا ہے ، مگر قاضی مقلد اگر ضعیف قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دے، تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوگا۔
اللہ پاک کی تعریف پر کتاب کا اختتام
علامہ شامی اخیر میں فرماتے ہیں کہ فتاویٰ نویسی کے جن اصولوں کو میں منظوم شکل میں بیان کر رہا تھا ، اس کا سلسلہ مکمل ہوا۔ اس پر میں اللہ پاک کی تعریف
Aun al-Mughni fi Hill 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. He said: In two situations there is scope for giving fatwa and acting on a weak opinion. First situation: A person is in extreme need, he has no choice but to adopt the weak opinion due to some compulsion, so such a compelled person can act on the weak opinion. For example: In the Hanafi school, according to both sides, for the obligation of ghusl it is sufficient that the semen moves from its place with desire, whether desire is present at the time of exiting the private part or not; this is the relied-upon (mufta bih) opinion. Imam Abu Yusuf says that for ghusl to be obligatory, it is necessary that the semen exits the private part with desire; this is a weak opinion. But if a traveler is in a place or on a transport where he would face difficulty in performing ghusl during travel, or he is a guest somewhere and feels shy to perform ghusl of janabah and fears accusation, then the jurists have permitted such a person that if at the time of ejaculation he holds his private part and does not let the semen exit, then when desire subsides, then if the semen exits, according to Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, ghusl will not be obligatory on him. Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion is not mufta bih, but due to necessity it was made mufta bih. Second situation: If a mufti has such strong ability of opinion and mature insight that he considers the weak opinion of the jurists to be strong on the basis of some other evidence, then in such a case he can act on the weak opinion of the jurists. Conclusion: In the level of compulsion, the mufti can himself act on the weak opinion and can also give fatwa to others. The correct Hanafi view in this regard is this. Deciding by weak opinion is absolutely not correct. As for the qadi, whether he can decide according to a weak opinion? Regarding this, Allama Shami (may Allah bless him) says: This permission is only for fatwa; as for judgment and decision, acting on a weak opinion is not correct. If the qadi is a mujtahid, it is necessary for him to decide according to the opinion he considers preponderant. If the qadi is a muqallid, it is necessary for him to decide according to the preponderant opinion of the madhhab, because they were bound to decide according to the preponderant opinion of the madhhab when they were entrusted with the office of qada. Therefore, both types of qadi must always decide according to the preponderant opinion. However, if a mujtahid qadi has decided according to a weak opinion, it will be executed, because the weak opinion becomes strong through the decision of the mujtahid qadi. But if a muqallid qadi decides according to a weak opinion, his decision will not be executed. End of the book with praise of Allah. Allama Shami says at the end: The series of principles of fatwa writing that I was explaining in poetic form has been completed. I praise Allah for this.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage from 'Aun al-Mughni' discusses the conditions under which a weak opinion can be used in fatwa and judgment. The text presents two scenarios for a mufti: first, when a person is in extreme necessity and cannot follow the strong opinion; second, when a mufti himself, through strong reasoning, comes to consider the weak opinion as strong. An example is given regarding ghusl: the relied-upon Hanafi view is that ghusl becomes obligatory when semen moves from its place with desire, regardless of whether desire is felt at exit. Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, requiring desire at exit, is weak. However, if a traveler faces difficulty or shame in performing ghusl, jurists permit him to hold his private part at ejaculation to prevent immediate exit; after desire subsides, if semen exits, ghusl is not obligatory according to Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion, which is adopted due to necessity. The passage then clarifies that this permission is only for fatwa, not for judgment. A qadi, whether mujtahid or muqallid, must decide by the preponderant opinion. If a mujtahid qadi decides by a weak opinion, his judgment is enforceable because his ijtihad strengthens it. But a muqallid qadi's decision by a weak opinion is not enforceable.

Key Terms
ضعیف قول (da'if qawl): An opinion that is not the relied-upon (mufta bih) view in the madhhab; it is weaker in evidence or authority.
راجح قول (rajih qawl): The preponderant opinion in the madhhab, considered stronger in evidence and authority.
قاضی مجتہد (qadi mujtahid): A judge who has the capacity to perform ijtihad and can weigh evidences independently.
قاضی مقلد (qadi muqallid): A judge who follows the madhhab and does not perform independent ijtihad; he must adhere to the rajih opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a mujtahid qadi decides a case based on a weak opinion, what is the status of his decision?
A) It is void because weak opinions cannot be used in judgment.
B) It is enforceable because his ijtihad makes the weak opinion strong.
C) It is valid only if the weak opinion was also the mufta bih.
D) It is suspended until approved by a higher court.

Key Takeaway
Weak opinions in the Hanafi school may be used in fatwa under necessity or if the mufti considers them strong, but in judgment only a mujtahid qadi can enforce such a decision.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Weak Opinion: Mufti vs Qadi in Hanafi Fiqh
Rasm al-Mufti rule: weak opinion use in fatwa vs judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction between mufti and qadi regarding weak opinions and identify when a judgment based on a weak opinion is enforceable.

Core Idea
A mufti may use a weak opinion in necessity; a qadi must always follow the rajih opinion, unless he is a mujtahid.

The Hanafi madhhab recognizes gradations of strength within its own opinions. While a mufti, in cases of necessity, can issue a fatwa based on a weaker view, a qadi (judge) is held to a stricter standard. This lesson dissects the ruling from Allamah Shami, clarifying the different obligations of a mufti, a mujtahid qadi, and a muqallid qadi when it comes to weak opinions.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the Three Roles
Identify the three legal actors: mufti (fatwa-giver), mujtahid qadi (independent judge), and muqallid qadi (bound judge). Each has a different scope for using weak opinions.
The passage focuses on the qadi's role, but the mufti's permission is also clarified.
2
State the Principle for Mufti
Extract the rule: In necessity (majburi), a mufti may both act upon and give fatwa based on a weak opinion. This is the correct Hanafi position.
Necessity is key; it is not an unrestricted permission.
3
State the Principle for Qadi
Extract the rule: A qadi (whether mujtahid or muqallid) is generally bound to judge by the strong (rajih) opinion. Weak opinions are not to be followed in judgments.
The exception for mujtahid qadi comes next.
4
Analyze the Exception for Mujtahid Qadi
If a mujtahid qadi judges by a weak opinion, his judgment becomes enforceable because his ijtihad strength transforms it into a strong ruling for that case. In contrast, a muqallid qadi's weak-based judgment is void.
This protects the judiciary's integrity by ensuring judgments are based on the strongest available evidence.
5
Synthesize the Full Rule
Combine all parts: Mufti – weak opinion permissible in necessity. Qadi mujtahid – must follow his own ijtihad but if he uses a weak opinion, it is enforceable. Qadi muqallid – must follow rajih of madhhab; weak opinion judgment is invalid.
This rule is a cornerstone of Hanafi ifta and qada methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاصل کلام
۱۰۹
مجبوری کے درجے میں ضعیف قول پر مفتی خود بھی عمل کر سکتا ہے، دوسروں کو بھی فتوی دے سکتا ہے، احناف کا صحیح قول اس سلسلے میں یہی ہے۔
قولِ ضعیف پر فیصلہ کرنا مطلقاً درست نہیں
رہی بات قاضی کی کہ وہ ضعیف قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کر سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟ تو اس سلسلے میں علامہ شامی صلى الله عليه وسلم فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ اجازت صرف فتوے کی حد تک ہے، جہاں تک قضا و فیصلے کی بات ہے، تو اس میں ضعیف قول پر عمل درست نہیں ۔ قاضی اگر مجتہد ہے، تو اُس پر لازم ہے کہ وہ اس قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرے، جو اُس کے نزدیک راجح ہے اور اگر قاضی مقلد ہے، تو اُس پر مذہب کے راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنا لازم ہے؛ کیوں کہ اُنھیں عہدہ قضاء سپر د کیے جانے کے وقت ، مذہب کے راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنے کا پابند کر دیا گیا ہے؛ لہذا دونوں طرح کے قاضی پر ہر حال میں راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنا لازم ہے؛ البتہ قاضی مجتہد نے اگر قولِ ضعیف کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دیا، تو وہ نافذ ہو جائے گا ؛ اس لیے کہ ضعیف قول قاضی مجتہد کے فیصلے سے قوی ہو جاتا ہے ، مگر قاضی مقلد اگر ضعیف قول کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دے، تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوگا۔
Synopsis: In the case of necessity, the mufti himself can act upon a weak opinion, and can also give fatwa to others. The correct Hanafi position in this regard is this. Ruling by weak opinion is absolutely not permissible. As for the qadi, can he judge according to a weak opinion or not? In this regard, Allamah Shami (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) says that this permission is only for fatwa; as for adjudication, acting upon a weak opinion is not correct. If the qadi is a mujtahid, it is binding upon him to judge according to the opinion that he considers strong. If the qadi is a muqallid, it is binding upon him to judge according to the strong opinion of the madhhab, because when he was entrusted with the office of qadi, he was made bound to judge according to the strong opinion of the madhhab. Thus, both types of qadi are obligated to judge according to the strong opinion in all circumstances. However, if a mujtahid qadi judges according to a weak opinion, his judgment will be enforceable, because the weak opinion becomes strong through the judgment of the mujtahid qadi. But if a muqallid qadi judges according to a weak opinion, his judgment will not be enforceable.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents a key rule in Hanafi ifta and qada. It distinguishes between the roles of a mufti and a qadi in relation to weak (da'if) opinions from the madhhab. For a mufti, in a situation of necessity (majburi), it is permissible to act upon a weak opinion and also to issue fatwa based on it. This is the correct (sahih) position in the Hanafi school. For a qadi, however, the rule is different. A qadi is not permitted to base his judgment on a weak opinion in absolute terms. If the qadi is a mujtahid, he must follow his own ijtihad and judge by what he deems strong. If he is a muqallid, he must judge by the strong opinion of his madhhab, as his appointment to the judiciary is conditional on this. The passage then gives an exception: if a mujtahid qadi issues a judgment based on a weak opinion, it becomes enforceable because his ijtihad authority elevates that opinion to strength in that particular case. But a muqallid qadi's judgment based on a weak opinion is null and void. This rule protects the integrity of the judiciary by ensuring that judgments are based on the strongest available evidence.

Key Terms
ضعیف قول (da'if qawl): A legal opinion within the Hanafi madhhab that is not considered the strongest, usually based on weaker evidence or lesser authority.
راجح قول (rajih qawl): The stronger, preferred opinion in the madhhab, which is given precedence in fatwa and judgment.
مفتی (mufti): One qualified to issue legal opinions (fatwa) based on the madhhab.
قاضی (qadi): A judge who renders binding decisions in disputes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a muqallid qadi who judges by a weak opinion?
A) His judgment is enforceable.
B) His judgment is not enforceable.
C) It is permissible but makruh.
D) It is valid only if the weak opinion is from the same madhhab.

Key Takeaway
A mufti may use a weak opinion in necessity; a qadi must abide by the strong opinion, but a mujtahid qadi's weak-opinion judgment becomes enforceable.
